<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Royal_Navy" title="Template:Royal Navy"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Royal_Navy" title="Template talk:Royal Navy"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Royal Navy</b> (<b>RN</b>) is the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">naval warfare force</a>. Although warships were used by the English kings from the early medieval period, the first major maritime engagements were fought in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hundred_Years_War" title="Hundred Years War">Hundred Years War</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a>. The modern Royal Navy traces its origins to the early 16th century; the oldest of the UK's armed services, it is known as the <b>Senior Service</b>.</p>
<p>From the middle decades of the 17th century and through the 18th century, the Royal Navy vied with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_Navy" title="Dutch Navy">Dutch Navy</a> and later with the <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">French Navy</a> for maritime supremacy. From the mid 18th century it was the world's most powerful navy until surpassed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. The Royal Navy played a key part in establishing the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">unmatched world power</a> during the 19th and first part of the 20th centuries. Due to this historical prominence, it is common, even among non-Britons, to refer to it as "the Royal Navy" without qualification.</p>
<p>Following <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the Royal Navy was significantly reduced in size,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[3]</a></sup> although at the onset of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> it was still the world's largest. By the end of the war, however, the United States Navy had emerged as the world's largest. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the Royal Navy transformed into a primarily <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare" title="Anti-submarine warfare">anti-submarine force</a>, hunting for <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> submarines, mostly active in the <a href="/wiki/GIUK_gap" title="GIUK gap">GIUK gap</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">collapse of the Soviet Union</a>, its focus has returned to <a href="/wiki/Expeditionary_warfare" title="Expeditionary warfare">expeditionary</a> operations <a href="/wiki/Standing_Royal_Navy_deployments" title="Standing Royal Navy deployments">around the world</a> and remains one of the world's foremost <a href="/wiki/Blue-water_navy" title="Blue-water navy">blue-water</a> navies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[6]</a></sup> However, reductions in naval spending have led to the Royal Navy suffering from multiple problems during the 21st century, including a personnel shortage and a reduction in the number of warships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Royal Navy maintains a fleet of technologically sophisticated ships and submarines<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[10]</a></sup> including an <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ocean_(L12)" title="HMS Ocean (L12)">amphibious assault ship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albion-class_landing_platform_dock" title="Albion-class landing platform dock">two amphibious transport docks</a>, four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanguard-class" title="Vanguard-class">ballistic missile submarines</a> (which maintain the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom" title="Nuclear weapons and the United Kingdom">UK's nuclear deterrent</a>), six <a href="/wiki/Fleet_submarine" title="Fleet submarine">nuclear fleet submarines</a>, six <a href="/wiki/Type_45_destroyer" title="Type 45 destroyer">guided missile destroyers</a>, thirteen <a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">frigates</a>, 15 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mine-countermeasure_vessel" title="Mine-countermeasure vessel">mine-countermeasure vessels</a> and 22 <a href="/wiki/Patrol_boat" title="Patrol boat">patrol vessels</a>. As of 19 March 2016, there are <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_Royal_Navy_ships" title="List of active Royal Navy ships">77 commissioned ships</a> (including submarines) in the Royal Navy, plus 9 ships of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Fleet_Auxiliary" title="Royal Fleet Auxiliary">Royal Fleet Auxiliary</a> (RFA); there are also five <a href="/wiki/Merchant_Navy_(United_Kingdom)" title="Merchant Navy (United Kingdom)">Merchant Navy ships</a> available to the RFA under a <a href="/wiki/Private_finance_initiative" title="Private finance initiative">private finance initiative</a>. The RFA replenishes Royal Navy warships at sea, and augments the Royal Navy's amphibious warfare capabilities through its three <a href="/wiki/Bay-class_landing_ship" title="Bay-class landing ship">Bay-class</a> landing ship vessels. It also works as a force multiplier for the Royal Navy, often doing patrols that frigates used to do. The total displacement of the Royal Navy is approximately 337,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonnes" title="Tonnes">tonnes</a> (603,000 tonnes including the Royal Fleet Auxiliary and Royal Marines).</p>
<p>The Royal Navy is part of <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Naval_Service" title="Her Majesty's Naval Service">Her Majesty's Naval Service</a>, which also includes the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a>. The professional head of the Naval Service is the <a href="/wiki/First_Sea_Lord" title="First Sea Lord">First Sea Lord</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Admiral_(United_Kingdom)" title="Admiral (United Kingdom)">admiral</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Defence Council of the United Kingdom">Defence Council of the United Kingdom</a>. The Defence Council delegates management of the Naval Service to the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Board_(United_Kingdom)" title="Admiralty Board (United Kingdom)">Admiralty Board</a>, chaired by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Defence" title="Secretary of State for Defence">Secretary of State for Defence</a>. The Royal Navy operates three bases in the United Kingdom where commissioned ships are based; <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Portsmouth" title="HMNB Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Clyde" title="HMNB Clyde">Clyde</a> and <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">Devonport</a>, the last being the largest operational naval base in Western Europe.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Role">Role</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Role">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As the seabourne branch of <a href="/wiki/British_Armed_Forces" title="British Armed Forces">HM Armed Forces</a>, the RN has various roles. As it stands today, the RN states its 6 major roles as detailed below as umbrella terms.</p>
<ul>
<li>Preventing Conflict - On a global and regional level</li>
<li>Providing Security At Sea - To ensure the stability of international trade at sea</li>
<li>International Partnerships - To help cement the relationship with the United Kingdom's allies (such as NATO)</li>
<li>Maintaining a Readiness To Fight - To protect the United Kingdom's interest across the globe</li>
<li>Protecting the Economy - To safe guard vital trade routes to guarantee the United Kingdom's and it's allies' economic prosperity at sea</li>
<li>Providing Humanitarian Aid - To deliver a fast and effective response to global catastrophes</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="History of the Royal Navy">History of the Royal Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Scots_Navy" title="Royal Scots Navy">Royal Scots Navy</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_of_an_English_navy">Development of an English navy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development of an English navy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The strength of the fleet of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> was an important element in the kingdom's power in the 10th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[11]</a></sup> At one point <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelred_the_Unready" title="Æthelred the Unready">Aethelred II</a> had an especially large fleet built by a national levy of one ship for every 310 <a href="/wiki/Hide_(unit)" title="Hide (unit)">hides</a> of land, but it is uncertain whether this was a standard or exceptional model for raising fleets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[12]</a></sup> During the period of Danish rule in the 11th century, the authorities maintained a standing fleet by taxation, and this continued for a time under the restored English regime of <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Confessor" title="Edward the Confessor">Edward the Confessor</a> (reigned 1042–1066), who frequently commanded fleets in person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[13]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BattleofSluys.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1560" data-file-width="1665" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BattleofSluys.jpeg/220px-BattleofSluys.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BattleofSluys.jpeg/330px-BattleofSluys.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BattleofSluys.jpeg/440px-BattleofSluys.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BattleofSluys.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sluys" title="Battle of Sluys">Battle of Sluys</a> as depicted in <a href="/wiki/Froissart%27s_Chronicles" title="Froissart's Chronicles">Froissart's Chronicles</a>; late 14th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>English naval power seemingly declined as a result of the Norman conquest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[14]</a></sup> Medieval fleets, in England as elsewhere, were almost entirely composed of merchant ships enlisted into naval service in time of war. From time to time a few "king's ships" owned by the monarch were built for specifically warlike purposes; but, unlike some European states, England did not maintain a small permanent core of warships in peacetime. England's naval organisation was haphazard and the mobilisation of fleets when war broke out was slow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the Viking era at an end, and conflict with France largely confined to the French lands of the English monarchy, England faced little threat from the sea during the 12th and 13th centuries, but in the 14th century the outbreak of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hundred_Years_War" title="Hundred Years War">Hundred Years War</a> dramatically increased the French menace. Early in the war French plans for an invasion of England failed when <a href="/wiki/Edward_III_of_England" title="Edward III of England">Edward III of England</a> destroyed the French fleet in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sluys" title="Battle of Sluys">Battle of Sluys</a> in 1340.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[16]</a></sup> Major fighting was thereafter confined to French soil and England's naval capabilities sufficed to transport armies and supplies safely to their continental destinations. However, while subsequent French invasion schemes came to nothing, England's naval forces could not prevent frequent raids on the south-coast ports by the French and their <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castilian</a> allies. Such raids halted finally only with the occupation of northern France by <a href="/wiki/Henry_V_of_England" title="Henry V of England">Henry V</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII</a> deserves a large share of credit in fostering sea power. He embarked on a program of building merchant ships larger than heretofore. He also invested in dockyards, and commissioned the oldest surviving <a href="/wiki/Dry_dock" title="Dry dock">dry dock</a> in 1495 at <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Portsmouth" title="HMNB Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="1500–1707"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1500.E2.80.931707">1500–1707</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1500–1707">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Invincible_Armada.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1956" data-file-width="2500" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Invincible_Armada.jpg/220px-Invincible_Armada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Invincible_Armada.jpg/330px-Invincible_Armada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Invincible_Armada.jpg/440px-Invincible_Armada.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Invincible_Armada.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A late 16th-century painting of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">Spanish Armada</a> in battle with English warships</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A standing "Navy Royal",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[19]</a></sup> with its own secretariat, dockyards and a permanent core of purpose-built warships, emerged during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[20]</a></sup> Under <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I</a> England became involved in a war with Spain, which saw privately owned vessels combining with the Queen's ships in highly profitable raids against Spanish commerce and colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1588, <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> sent the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">Spanish Armada</a> against England to end English support for Dutch rebels, to stop English <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">corsair</a> activity and to depose the Protestant Elizabeth I and restore Catholicism to England. The Spaniards sailed from <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, planning to escort an invasion force from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Netherlands" title="Spanish Netherlands">Spanish Netherlands</a> but the scheme failed due to poor planning, English harrying, blocking action by the Dutch, and severe storms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[22]</a></sup> A major English expedition the following year was intended by Elizabeth to destroy the survivors of the Spanish fleet, but instead dissipated its efforts in unsuccessful schemes to intercept a Spanish treasure convoy or foment revolt against Spanish rule in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>.</p>
<p>During the early 17th century, England's relative naval power deteriorated, and there were increasing raids by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbary_corsairs" title="Barbary corsairs">Barbary corsairs</a> on ships and English coastal communities to capture people as <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>, which the Navy had little success in countering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a> undertook a major programme of warship building, creating a small force of powerful ships, but his methods of fund-raising to finance the fleet contributed to the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[24]</a></sup> In the wake of this conflict and the abolition of the monarchy, the new <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_England" title="Commonwealth of England">Commonwealth of England</a>, isolated and threatened from all sides, dramatically expanded the Navy, which became the most powerful in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Scheveningen_(Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde)(Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3680" data-file-width="5950" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Scheveningen_(Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde)(Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Scheveningen" title="Battle of Scheveningen">Battle of Scheveningen</a> in 1653</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The new regime's introduction of <a href="/wiki/Navigation_Acts" title="Navigation Acts">Navigation Acts</a>, providing that all merchant shipping to and from England or her colonies should be carried out by English ships, led to war with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[26]</a></sup> In the early stages of this <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="First Anglo-Dutch War">First Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1652–1654), the superiority of the large, heavily armed English ships was offset by superior Dutch tactical organisation and the fighting was inconclusive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[27]</a></sup> English tactical improvements resulted in a series of crushing victories in 1653 at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Portland" title="Battle of Portland">Portland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Gabbard" title="Battle of the Gabbard">the Gabbard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Scheveningen" title="Battle of Scheveningen">Scheveningen</a>, bringing peace on favourable terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[28]</a></sup> This was the first war fought largely, on the English side, by purpose-built, state-owned warships. It was followed by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1654-1660)" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1654-1660)">war with Spain</a>, which saw the English conquest of <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> in 1655 and successful attacks on Spanish treasure fleets in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cadiz_(1656)" title="Battle of Cadiz (1656)">1656</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_(1657)" title="Battle of Santa Cruz de Tenerife (1657)">1657</a>, but also the devastation of English merchant shipping by the <a href="/wiki/Dunkirkers" title="Dunkirkers">privateers of Dunkirk</a>, until their home port was captured by Anglo-French forces in 1658.</p>
<p>The English monarchy was restored in May 1660, and <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> assumed the throne. One of his first acts was to re-establish the Navy, but from this point on, it ceased to be the personal possession of the reigning monarch, and instead became a national institution – with the title of "The Royal Navy".</p>
<p>As a result of their defeat in the First Anglo-Dutch War, the Dutch transformed their navy, largely abandoning the use of militarised merchantmen and establishing a fleet composed mainly of heavily armed, purpose-built warships, as the English had done previously. Consequently, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Second Anglo-Dutch War">Second Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1665–1667) was a closely fought struggle between evenly matched opponents, with English victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lowestoft" title="Battle of Lowestoft">Lowestoft</a> (1665) countered by Dutch triumph in the epic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four_Days_Battle" title="Four Days Battle">Four Days Battle</a> (1666).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[29]</a></sup> The deadlock was broken not by combat but by the superiority of Dutch public finance, as in 1667 Charles II was forced to lay up the fleet in port for lack of money to keep it at sea, while negotiating for peace. Disaster followed, as the Dutch fleet mounted the <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_the_Medway" title="Raid on the Medway">Raid on the Medway</a>, breaking into <a href="/wiki/Chatham_Dockyard" title="Chatham Dockyard">Chatham Dockyard</a> and capturing or burning many of the Navy's largest ships at their moorings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[30]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Third Anglo-Dutch War">Third Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1672–1674), Charles II allied with <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV of France</a> against the Dutch, but the combined Anglo-French fleet was fought to a standstill in a series of inconclusive battles, while the French invasion by land was warded off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_(Peter_van_de_Velde).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1294" data-file-width="1974" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg/220px-Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg/330px-Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg/440px-Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_(Peter_van_de_Velde).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Dutch <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_the_Medway" title="Raid on the Medway">Raid on the Medway</a> in 1667 during the Second Anglo–Dutch War</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the 1670s and 1680s, the Navy succeeded in permanently ending the threat to English shipping from the Barbary corsairs, inflicting defeats which induced the Barbary states to conclude long-lasting peace treaties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[32]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> of 1688, England joined the European coalition against Louis XIV in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_the_Grand_Alliance" title="War of the Grand Alliance">War of the Grand Alliance</a> (1688–1697). Louis' recent shipbuilding programme had given France the largest navy in Europe. A combined Anglo-Dutch fleet was defeated at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Beachy_Head_(1690)" title="Battle of Beachy Head (1690)">Beachy Head</a> (1690), but victory at <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Barfleur_and_La_Hogue" title="Battles of Barfleur and La Hogue">Barfleur-La Hogue</a> (1692) was a turning-point, marking the end of France's brief pre-eminence at sea and the beginning of an enduring English, later British, supremacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the course of the 17th century, the Navy completed the transition from a semi-amateur Navy Royal fighting in conjunction with private vessels into a fully professional institution. Its financial provisions were gradually regularised, it came to rely on dedicated warships only, and it developed a professional officer corps with a defined career structure, superseding an earlier mix of "gentlemen" (upper-class soldiers) and "tarpaulins" (professional seamen, who generally served on merchant or fishing vessels in peacetime).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Development_of_Britain's_navy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_of_Britain.27s_navy">Development of Britain's navy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Development of Britain's navy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="1707–1815"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1707.E2.80.931815">1707–1815</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1707–1815">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2952" data-file-width="2250" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg/170px-HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg/255px-HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg/340px-HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Victory" title="HMS Victory">HMS <i>Victory</i></a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson" title="Horatio Nelson">Nelson</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Trafalgar</a>, is still a <a href="/wiki/Ship_commissioning" title="Ship commissioning">commissioned</a> Royal Navy ship, although she is now permanently kept in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dry-dock" title="Dry-dock">dry-dock</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 1707 <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union</a>, which created the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> in 1707, established the Royal Navy of the newly united kingdom by the merger of the three-ship <a href="/wiki/Royal_Scots_Navy" title="Royal Scots Navy">Royal Scots Navy</a> with the Royal Navy of England. Throughout the 18th and 19th centuries, the Royal Navy was the largest maritime force in the world, but until 1805 combinations of enemies repeatedly matched or exceeded its forces in numbers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[35]</a></sup> Despite this, it was able to maintain an almost uninterrupted ascendancy over its rivals through superiority in financing, tactics, training, organisation, social cohesion, hygiene, dockyard facilities, logistical support and (from the middle of the 18th century) warship design and construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> (1702–1714), the Navy operated in conjunction with the Dutch against the navies of France and Spain, in support of the efforts of Britain's Austrian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> allies to seize control of Spain and its Mediterranean dependencies from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bourbons" title="Bourbons">Bourbons</a>. Amphibious operations by the Anglo-Dutch fleet brought about the capture of <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> and a number of Spanish mainland ports, most importantly <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. While most of these gains were turned over to the Habsburgs, Britain held on to <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a>, which were retained in the peace settlement, providing the Navy with Mediterranean bases. Early in the war French naval squadrons had done considerable damage to English and Dutch commercial convoys. However, a major victory over France and Spain at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vigo_Bay" title="Battle of Vigo Bay">Vigo Bay</a> (1702), further successes in battle, and the scuttling of the entire French Mediterranean fleet at <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a> in 1707 virtually cleared the Navy's opponents from the seas for the latter part of the war. Naval operations also enabled the conquest of the French colonies in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[37]</a></sup> Further conflict with Spain followed in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Quadruple_Alliance" title="War of the Quadruple Alliance">War of the Quadruple Alliance</a> (1718–1720), in which the Navy helped thwart a Spanish attempt to regain <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> from Austria and <a href="/wiki/Savoy" title="Savoy">Savoy</a>, defeating a Spanish fleet at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cape_Passaro" title="Battle of Cape Passaro">Cape Passaro</a> (1718), and in an undeclared war in the 1720s, in which Spain tried to retake Gibraltar and Menorca.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LindsayCambridge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="952" data-file-width="1280" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/220px-LindsayCambridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/330px-LindsayCambridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/440px-LindsayCambridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LindsayCambridge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_expedition_against_Cuba" title="British expedition against Cuba">British expedition against Cuba</a> in 1762</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After a period of relative peace, the Navy became engaged in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins' Ear">War of Jenkins' Ear</a> (1739–1748) against Spain, which was dominated by a series of costly and mostly unsuccessful attacks on Spanish ports in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, primarily a huge expedition against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartagena_de_Indias" title="Cartagena de Indias">Cartagena de Indias</a> in 1741. These led to heavy loss of life from tropical diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[40]</a></sup> In 1742 the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Kingdom of the Two Sicilies">Kingdom of the Two Sicilies</a> was driven to withdraw from the war in the space of half an hour by the threat of a bombardment of its capital <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a> by a small British squadron. The war became subsumed in the wider <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> (1744–1748), once again pitting Britain against France. Naval fighting in this war, which for the first time included major operations in the Indian Ocean, was largely inconclusive, the most significant event being the failure of <a href="/wiki/Planned_French_invasion_of_Britain_(1744)" title="Planned French invasion of Britain (1744)">an attempted French invasion of England</a> in 1744.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The subsequent <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> (1756–1763) saw the Navy conduct amphibious campaigns leading to the conquest of French Canada, of French colonies in the Caribbean and West Africa and of small islands off the French coast, while operations in the Indian Ocean contributed to the destruction of French power in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[42]</a></sup> A new French <a href="/wiki/Planned_French_invasion_of_Britain_(1759)" title="Planned French invasion of Britain (1759)">attempt to invade Britain</a> was thwarted by the defeat of their escort fleet in the extraordinary <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Quiberon_Bay" title="Battle of Quiberon Bay">Battle of Quiberon Bay</a> in 1759, fought in a gale on a dangerous <a href="/wiki/Lee_shore" title="Lee shore">lee shore</a>. Once again the British fleet effectively eliminated the French Navy from the war, leading France to abandon major operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[43]</a></sup> In 1762 the resumption of hostilities with Spain led to the British capture of <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, along with a Spanish fleet sheltering there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[44]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="589" data-file-width="1024" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg/250px-The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg/375px-The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg/500px-The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Saintes" title="Battle of the Saintes">Battle of the Saintes</a> (1782). On the right, the French flagship, the <i><a href="/wiki/French_ship_Ville_de_Paris_(1764)" title="French ship Ville de Paris (1764)">Ville de Paris</a></i>, in action against <a href="/wiki/HMS_Barfleur_(1768)" title="HMS Barfleur (1768)">HMS <i>Barfleur</i></a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_War_of_Independence" title="American War of Independence">American War of Independence</a> (1775–1783) the Royal Navy readily obliterated the small <a href="/wiki/Continental_Navy" title="Continental Navy">Continental Navy</a> of frigates fielded by the rebel colonists, but the entry of France, Spain and the Netherlands into the war against Britain produced a combination of opposing forces which deprived the Navy of its position of superiority for the first time since the 1690s, briefly but decisively. The war saw a series of inconclusive battles in the Atlantic and Caribbean, in which the Navy failed to achieve the decisive victories needed to secure the supply lines of British forces in North America and to cut off the colonial rebels from outside support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[45]</a></sup> The most important operation of the war came in 1781 when, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Chesapeake" title="Battle of the Chesapeake">Battle of the Chesapeake</a>, the British fleet failed to lift the French blockade of Lord Cornwallis's army, resulting in Cornwallis's surrender at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yorktown_(1781)" title="Battle of Yorktown (1781)">Yorktown</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[46]</a></sup> Although this disaster effectively concluded the fighting in North America, hostilities continued in the Indian Ocean, where the French were prevented from re-establishing a meaningful foothold in India, and in the Caribbean. British victory in the Caribbean in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Saintes" title="Battle of the Saintes">Battle of the Saintes</a> in 1782 and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cape_Spartel" title="Battle of Cape Spartel">relief of Gibraltar</a> later the same year symbolised the restoration of British naval ascendancy, but this came too late to prevent the independence of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1502" data-file-width="2102" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg/220px-Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg/330px-Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg/440px-Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">Bombardment of Algiers</a> in 1816 to support the ultimatum to release European slaves</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The eradication of scurvy from the Royal Navy in the 1790s came about due to the efforts of <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Blane" title="Gilbert Blane">Gilbert Blane</a>, chairman of the Navy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sick_and_Hurt_Board" title="Sick and Hurt Board">Sick and Hurt Board</a>, which ordered fresh lemon juice to be given to sailors on ships. Other navies soon adopted this successful solution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a> (1793–1801) and <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> (1803–1814 and 1815) saw the Royal Navy reach a peak of efficiency, dominating the navies of all Britain's adversaries, which spent most of the war blockaded in port. The Navy achieved an emphatic early victory at the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_First_of_June" title="Glorious First of June">Glorious First of June</a> (1794), and gained a number of smaller victories while supporting abortive French Royalist efforts to regain control of France. In the course of one such operation, the majority of the French Mediterranean fleet was captured or destroyed during a short-lived occupation of Toulon in 1793.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[49]</a></sup> The military successes of the French Revolutionary régime brought the Spanish and Dutch navies into the war on the French side, but the losses inflicted on the Dutch at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Camperdown" title="Battle of Camperdown">Battle of Camperdown</a> in 1797 and the surrender of their surviving fleet to a landing force at Den Helder in 1799 effectively eliminated the Dutch navy from the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[50]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Spithead_and_Nore_mutinies" title="Spithead and Nore mutinies">Spithead and Nore mutinies</a> in 1797 incapacitated the Channel and North Sea fleets, leaving Britain potentially exposed to invasion, but were rapidly resolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[51]</a></sup> The British Mediterranean fleet under <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson,_1st_Viscount_Nelson" title="Horatio Nelson, 1st Viscount Nelson">Horatio Nelson</a> failed to intercept <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a>'s 1798 expedition to invade Egypt, but annihilated the French fleet at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Nile" title="Battle of the Nile">Battle of the Nile</a>, leaving Bonaparte's army isolated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[52]</a></sup> The emergence of a Baltic coalition opposed to Britain led to an attack on Denmark, which lost much of its fleet in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Copenhagen_(1801)" title="Battle of Copenhagen (1801)">Battle of Copenhagen</a> (1801) and came to terms with Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[53]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trafalgar1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="645" data-file-width="1200" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Trafalgar1.jpg/280px-Trafalgar1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Trafalgar1.jpg/420px-Trafalgar1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Trafalgar1.jpg/560px-Trafalgar1.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trafalgar1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a>, depicted here in its opening phase</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During these years, the Navy also conducted amphibious operations that captured most of the French Caribbean islands and the Dutch colonies at the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylon" title="Ceylon">Ceylon</a>. Though successful in their outcome, the expeditions to the Caribbean, conducted on a grand scale, led to devastating losses from disease. Except for Ceylon and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>, these gains were returned following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_of_Amiens" title="Peace of Amiens">Peace of Amiens</a> in 1802, which briefly halted the fighting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[54]</a></sup> Menorca, which had been repeatedly lost and regained during the 18th century, was restored to Spain, its place as the Navy's main base in the Mediterranean being taken by the new acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>. War resumed in 1803 and Napoleon attempted to assemble a large enough fleet from the French and Spanish squadrons blockaded in various ports to cover an invasion of England. The Navy frustrated these efforts, and following the abandonment of the invasion plan, Nelson defeated the combined Franco-Spanish fleet at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Trafalgar</a> (1805).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[55]</a></sup> This victory marked the culmination of decades of developing British naval dominance, and left the Navy in a position of uncontested hegemony at sea which endured until the early years of the 20th century.</p>
<p>After Trafalgar, large-scale fighting at sea remained limited to the destruction of small, fugitive French squadrons, and amphibious operations which again captured the colonies which had been restored at Amiens, along with France's Indian Ocean base at <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moluccas" title="Moluccas">Moluccas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[56]</a></sup> In 1807 French plans to seize the Danish fleet led to a pre-emptive British <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Copenhagen_(1807)" title="Battle of Copenhagen (1807)">attack on Copenhagen</a>, resulting in the surrender of the entire Danish navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[57]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Impressment" title="Impressment">impressment</a> of British and American sailors from American ships contributed to the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> (1812–1814) against the United States, in which the naval fighting was largely confined to commerce raiding and single-ship actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[58]</a></sup> The brief renewal of war after <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s return to power in 1815 did not bring a resumption of naval combat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="1815–1914"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1815.E2.80.931914">1815–1914</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1815–1914">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Between 1815 and 1914, the Navy saw little serious action, owing to the absence of any opponent strong enough to challenge its dominance. During this period, naval warfare underwent a comprehensive transformation, brought about by steam propulsion, metal ship construction, and explosive munitions. Despite having to completely replace its war fleet, the Navy managed to maintain its overwhelming advantage over all potential rivals. Due to British leadership in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, the country enjoyed unparalleled shipbuilding capacity and financial resources, which ensured that no rival could take advantage of these revolutionary changes to negate the British advantage in ship numbers.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9,137_tons,_Royal_Navy_(first_armour-plated,_iron-hulled_warship.)_(11632529933).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1084" data-file-width="1619" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg/220px-HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg/330px-HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg/440px-HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9,137_tons,_Royal_Navy_(first_armour-plated,_iron-hulled_warship.)_(11632529933).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Warrior_(1860)" title="HMS Warrior (1860)">HMS <i>Warrior</i></a>, the first iron-hulled, armour-plated warship</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1859, the fleet was estimated to number about 1000 in all, including both combat and non-combat vessels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[60]</a></sup> In 1889, Parliament passed the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Defence_Act_1889" title="Naval Defence Act 1889">Naval Defence Act</a>, which formally adopted the 'two-power standard', which stipulated that the Royal Navy should maintain a number of battleships at least equal to the combined strength of the next two largest navies.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_ships_in_Canton.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1383" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/British_ships_in_Canton.jpg/220px-British_ships_in_Canton.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/British_ships_in_Canton.jpg/330px-British_ships_in_Canton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/British_ships_in_Canton.jpg/440px-British_ships_in_Canton.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_ships_in_Canton.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The British assault on <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Canton</a> during the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a> in 1841</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first major action that the Royal Navy saw during this period was the <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">Bombardment of Algiers</a> in 1816 by a joint Anglo-Dutch fleet under <a href="/wiki/Edward_Pellew,_1st_Viscount_Exmouth" title="Edward Pellew, 1st Viscount Exmouth">Lord Exmouth</a>, to force the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbary_states" title="Barbary states">Barbary state</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regency_of_Algiers" title="Regency of Algiers">Algiers</a> to free Christian slaves and to halt the practice of enslaving Europeans. During the <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">Greek War of Independence</a>, the combined navies of Britain, France and Russia defeated an Ottoman fleet at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Navarino" title="Battle of Navarino">Battle of Navarino</a> in 1827, the last major action between sailing ships. During the same period, the Royal Navy took anti-piracy actions in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[61]</a></sup> Between 1807 and 1865, it maintained a <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_Africa" title="Blockade of Africa">Blockade of Africa</a> to counter the illegal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a>. It also participated in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> of 1854–56, as well as numerous military actions throughout Asia and Africa, notably the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Opium_War" title="Second Opium War">Second Opium Wars</a> with <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> China. On 27 August 1896, the Royal Navy took part in the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Zanzibar_War" title="Anglo-Zanzibar War">Anglo-Zanzibar War</a>, which was the shortest war in history.</p>
<p>The end of the 19th century saw structural changes brought about by the <a href="/wiki/First_Sea_Lord" title="First Sea Lord">First Sea Lord</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Fisher,_1st_Baron_Fisher" title="John Fisher, 1st Baron Fisher">Jackie Fisher</a>, who retired, scrapped or placed into reserve many of the older vessels, making funds and manpower available for newer ships. He also oversaw the development of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Dreadnought_(1906)" title="HMS Dreadnought (1906)">HMS <i>Dreadnought</i></a>, launched in 1906. Its speed and firepower rendered all existing battleships obsolete. The industrial and economic development of <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a> had by this time overtaken Britain, enabling the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_German_Navy" title="Imperial German Navy">Imperial German Navy</a> to attempt to outpace British construction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dreadnoughts" title="Dreadnoughts">dreadnoughts</a>. In the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Anglo-German_naval_arms_race" title="Anglo-German naval arms race">arms race</a>, Britain succeeded in maintaining a substantial numerical advantage over Germany, but for the first time since 1805 another navy now existed with the capacity to challenge the Royal Navy in battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Reforms were also gradually introduced in the conditions for enlisted men with the abolition of military <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flogging" title="Flogging">flogging</a> in 1879, amongst others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[63]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Dreadnought_1906_H61017.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="558" data-file-width="740" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/HMS_Dreadnought_1906_H61017.jpg/220px-HMS_Dreadnought_1906_H61017.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/HMS_Dreadnought_1906_H61017.jpg/330px-HMS_Dreadnought_1906_H61017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/HMS_Dreadnought_1906_H61017.jpg/440px-HMS_Dreadnought_1906_H61017.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Dreadnought_1906_H61017.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Dreadnought_(1906)" title="HMS Dreadnought (1906)">HMS <i>Dreadnought</i></a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span id="1914–1945"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1914.E2.80.931945">1914–1945</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1914–1945">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>, most of the Royal Navy's strength was mostly deployed at home in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Grand_Fleet" title="British Grand Fleet">Grand Fleet</a>, confronting the German <a href="/wiki/High_Seas_Fleet" title="High Seas Fleet">High Seas Fleet</a> across the North Sea. Several inconclusive clashes took place between them, chiefly the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jutland" title="Battle of Jutland">Battle of Jutland</a> in 1916. The British numerical advantage proved insurmountable, leading the High Seas Fleet to abandon any attempt to challenge British dominance.</p>
<p>Elsewhere in the world, the Navy hunted down the handful of German surface raiders at large. During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dardanelles_Campaign" title="Dardanelles Campaign">Dardanelles Campaign</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in 1915, it suffered heavy losses during a failed attempt to break through the system of minefields and shore batteries defending the straits.</p>
<p>Upon entering the war, the Navy had immediately established a <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_Germany" title="Blockade of Germany">blockade of Germany</a>. The Navy's <a href="/wiki/Northern_Patrol" title="Northern Patrol">Northern Patrol</a> closed off access to the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Dover_Patrol" title="Dover Patrol">Dover Patrol</a> closed off access to the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>. The Navy also mined the North Sea. As well as closing off the Imperial German Navy's access to the Atlantic, the blockade largely blocked neutral merchant shipping heading to or from Germany. The blockade was maintained during the eight months after the armistice was agreed to force Germany to end the war and sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most serious menace faced by the Navy came from the attacks on merchant shipping mounted by German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U-boats" title="U-boats">U-boats</a>. For much of the war this submarine campaign was restricted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prize_rules" title="Prize rules">prize rules</a> requiring merchant ships to be warned and evacuated before sinking. In 1915, the Germans renounced these restrictions and began to sink merchant ships on sight, but later returned to the previous <a href="/wiki/Rules_of_engagement" title="Rules of engagement">rules of engagement</a> to placate neutral opinion. A resumption of unrestricted submarine warfare in 1917 raised the prospect of Britain and its allies being starved into submission. The Navy's response to this new form of warfare had proved inadequate due to its refusal to adopt a <a href="/wiki/Convoy" title="Convoy">convoy</a> system for merchant shipping, despite the demonstrated effectiveness of the technique in protecting troop ships. The belated introduction of convoys sharply reduced losses and brought the U-boat threat under control.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Ark_Royal_h85716.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2130" data-file-width="3200" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/HMS_Ark_Royal_h85716.jpg/220px-HMS_Ark_Royal_h85716.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/HMS_Ark_Royal_h85716.jpg/330px-HMS_Ark_Royal_h85716.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/HMS_Ark_Royal_h85716.jpg/440px-HMS_Ark_Royal_h85716.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Ark_Royal_h85716.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Ark_Royal_(91)" title="HMS Ark Royal (91)">HMS <i>Ark Royal</i></a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the inter-war period, the Royal Navy was stripped of much of its power. The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Naval_Treaty" title="Washington Naval Treaty">Washington</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Naval_Treaty" title="London Naval Treaty">London</a> Naval Treaties imposed the scrapping of some capital ships and limitations on new construction. In 1932, the <a href="/wiki/Invergordon_Mutiny" title="Invergordon Mutiny">Invergordon Mutiny</a> took place over a proposed 25% pay cut, which was eventually reduced to 10%. International tensions increased in the mid-1930s and the <a href="/wiki/Second_London_Naval_Treaty" title="Second London Naval Treaty">Second London Naval Treaty</a> of 1935 failed to halt the development of a naval <a href="/wiki/Arms_race" title="Arms race">arms race</a>. By 1938, treaty limits were effectively being ignored. The re-armament of the Royal Navy was well under way by this point; the Royal Navy had begun construction of the still treaty-affected and undergunned <a href="/wiki/King_George_V-class_battleship_(1939)" title="King George V-class battleship (1939)">new battleships</a> and its first full-sized purpose-built aircraft carriers. In addition to new construction, several existing old battleships (whose gun power offset to a significant extent the weakly armed new battleships), battlecruisers and heavy cruisers were reconstructed, and anti-aircraft weaponry reinforced, while new technologies, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASDIC" title="ASDIC">ASDIC</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huff-Duff" title="Huff-Duff">Huff-Duff</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydrophones" title="Hydrophones">hydrophones</a>, were developed. The Navy had lost control of naval aviation when the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Air_Service" title="Royal Naval Air Service">Royal Naval Air Service</a> was merged with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Flying_Corps" title="Royal Flying Corps">Royal Flying Corps</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> in 1918, but regained control of ship-board aircraft with the return of the <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Air_Arm" title="Fleet Air Arm">Fleet Air Arm</a> to Naval control in 1937. However, the effectiveness of its aircraft lagged far behind its rivals, and around this time the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Navy" title="Imperial Japanese Navy">Imperial Japanese Navy</a> and the United States Navy began to surpass the Royal Navy in air power.</p>
<p>At the start of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> in 1939, the Royal Navy was the largest in the world, with over 1,400 vessels, including:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[66]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>7 aircraft carriers - with 5 more under construction</li>
<li>15 battleships and battlecruisers - with 5 more under construction</li>
<li>66 cruisers - with 23 more under construction</li>
<li>184 destroyers - with 52 under construction</li>
<li>45 escort and patrol vessels - with 9 under construction and one on order</li>
<li>60 submarines - with 9 under construction</li>
</ul>
<p>During the early phases of the Second World War, the Royal Navy provided critical cover during British evacuations from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Dynamo" title="Operation Dynamo">Dunkirk</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Taranto" title="Battle of Taranto">Taranto</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrew_Browne_Cunningham,_1st_Viscount_Cunningham_of_Hyndhope" title="Andrew Browne Cunningham, 1st Viscount Cunningham of Hyndhope">Admiral Cunningham</a> commanded a fleet that launched the first all-aircraft naval attack in history. Later, Cunningham was determined that as many Allied soldiers as possible should be evacuated after their <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Crete" title="Battle of Crete">defeat on Crete</a>. When army generals feared he would lose too many ships, he famously said, "It takes the Navy three years to build a new ship. It will take three hundred years to build a new tradition. The evacuation will continue."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Churchill265_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Churchill265-72">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Battlecruiser_HMS_Hood_circa_1932.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="456" data-file-width="740" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/British_Battlecruiser_HMS_Hood_circa_1932.jpg/220px-British_Battlecruiser_HMS_Hood_circa_1932.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/British_Battlecruiser_HMS_Hood_circa_1932.jpg/330px-British_Battlecruiser_HMS_Hood_circa_1932.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/British_Battlecruiser_HMS_Hood_circa_1932.jpg/440px-British_Battlecruiser_HMS_Hood_circa_1932.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Battlecruiser_HMS_Hood_circa_1932.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
British battlecruiser <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HMS_Hood_(51)" title="HMS Hood (51)">HMS <i>Hood</i></a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Royal Navy suffered heavy <a href="/wiki/List_of_Royal_Navy_losses_in_World_War_II" title="List of Royal Navy losses in World War II">losses</a> in the first two years of the war, including the carriers HMS <a href="/wiki/HMS_Courageous_(50)" title="HMS Courageous (50)"><i>Courageous</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Glorious" title="HMS Glorious"><i>Glorious</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ark_Royal_(91)" title="HMS Ark Royal (91)"><i>Ark Royal</i></a>, the battleships HMS <a href="/wiki/HMS_Royal_Oak_(08)" title="HMS Royal Oak (08)"><i>Royal Oak</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Barham_(04)" title="HMS Barham (04)"><i>Barham</i></a> and the battlecruiser HMS <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HMS_Hood_(51)" title="HMS Hood (51)"><i>Hood</i></a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Theatre_of_World_War_II" title="European Theatre of World War II">European Theatre</a>, and the carrier HMS <a href="/wiki/HMS_Hermes_(95)" title="HMS Hermes (95)"><i>Hermes</i></a>, the battleship HMS <a href="/wiki/HMS_Prince_of_Wales_(53)" title="HMS Prince of Wales (53)"><i>Prince of Wales</i></a>, the battlecruiser HMS <a href="/wiki/HMS_Repulse_(1916)" title="HMS Repulse (1916)"><i>Repulse</i></a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heavy_cruisers" title="Heavy cruisers">heavy cruisers</a> HMS <a href="/wiki/HMS_Exeter_(68)" title="HMS Exeter (68)"><i>Exeter</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Dorsetshire_(40)" title="HMS Dorsetshire (40)"><i>Dorsetshire</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Cornwall_(56)" title="HMS Cornwall (56)"><i>Cornwall</i></a> in the Asian Theatre. Of the 1,418 men on the <i>Hood</i>, only three survived its sinking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[68]</a></sup> Over 3,000 people were lost when the converted <a href="/wiki/Troopship" title="Troopship">troopship</a> <i><a href="/wiki/RMS_Lancastria" title="RMS Lancastria">Lancastria</a></i> was sunk in June 1940, the greatest maritime disaster in Britain's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[69]</a></sup> There were however also successes against enemy surface ships, as in the battles of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_River_Plate" title="Battle of the River Plate">the River Plate</a> in 1939, <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Narvik" title="Battles of Narvik">Narvik</a> in 1940 and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cape_Matapan" title="Battle of Cape Matapan">Cape Matapan</a> in 1941, and the sinking of the German capital ships <i><a href="/wiki/German_battleship_Bismarck" title="German battleship Bismarck">Bismarck</a></i> in 1941 and <i><a href="/wiki/German_battleship_Scharnhorst" title="German battleship Scharnhorst">Scharnhorst</a></i> in 1943.</p>
<p>The Navy's most critical struggle in this war was the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a>, the defence of Britain's vital Atlantic supply lines against U-boat attack. While a convoy system was instituted from the start of the war, German submarine tactics, based on group attacks by "wolf-packs", were much more effective than in the previous war, and the threat remained serious for well over three years. Defences were strengthened by the deployment of purpose-built escorts, of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Escort_carriers" title="Escort carriers">escort carriers</a>, of long-range patrol aircraft and of improved anti-submarine weapons and sensors, and by the deciphering of German signals by the code-breakers of <a href="/wiki/Bletchley_Park" title="Bletchley Park">Bletchley Park</a>. The threat was at last effectively broken by devastating losses inflicted on the U-boats in the spring of 1943. Intense convoy battles of a different sort, against combined air, surface and submarine threats, were fought off enemy-controlled coasts in <a href="/wiki/Arctic_convoys_of_World_War_II" title="Arctic convoys of World War II">the Arctic</a>, where Britain ran supply convoys through to Russia, and in the Mediterranean, where the struggle focused on <a href="/wiki/Malta_convoys" title="Malta convoys">sustaining the key British outpost of Malta</a>.</p>
<p>The Navy was vital in guarding the sea lanes that enabled British forces to fight in remote parts of the world such as North Africa, the Mediterranean and the Far East. Naval supremacy was also essential to amphibious operations such as the invasions of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Torch" title="Operation Torch">Northwest Africa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Husky" title="Operation Husky">Sicily</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy" title="Allied invasion of Italy">Italy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Normandy</a>. By the end of the war the Royal Navy comprised over 4,800 ships, and was the second largest fleet in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Postwar_period_and_early_21st_century">Postwar period and early 21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Postwar period and early 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After the Second World War, the decline of the British Empire and the economic hardships in Britain forced the reduction in the size and capability of the Royal Navy. All of the pre-war ships (except for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_class_cruiser_(1936)" title="Town class cruiser (1936)">Town-class</a> light cruisers) were quickly retired and most sold for scrapping over the years 1945–48, and only the best condition ships (the four surviving KG-V class battleships, carriers, cruisers, and some destroyers) were retained and refitted for service. The increasingly powerful United States Navy took on the former role of the Royal Navy as global naval power and police force of the sea. The combination of the threat of the Soviet Union, and Britain's commitments throughout the world, created a new role for the Navy. Governments since the Second World War have had to balance commitments with increasing budgetary pressures, partly due to the increasing cost of weapons systems, what historian <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kennedy" title="Paul Kennedy">Paul Kennedy</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Upward_Spiral" title="Upward Spiral">Upward Spiral</a>. These pressures have been exacerbated by bitter inter-service rivalry. A modest new construction programme was initiated with some new carriers (<a href="/wiki/1942_Design_Light_Fleet_Carrier" title="1942 Design Light Fleet Carrier"><i>Majestic</i>-</a> and <a href="/wiki/Centaur-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Centaur-class aircraft carrier"><i>Centaur</i>-class</a> light carriers, and <a href="/wiki/Audacious-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Audacious-class aircraft carrier"><i>Audacious</i>-class</a> large carriers being completed between 1948 through 1958), along with three <a href="/wiki/Tiger-class_cruiser" title="Tiger-class cruiser"><i>Tiger</i>-class</a> cruisers (completed 1959–61), the <a href="/wiki/Daring-class_destroyer_(1949)" title="Daring-class destroyer (1949)"><i>Daring</i>-class destroyers</a> in the 1950s, and finally the <a href="/wiki/County-class_destroyer" title="County-class destroyer">County-class</a> guided missile destroyers completed in the 1960s.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanguard_at_Faslane_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1921" data-file-width="2547" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Vanguard_at_Faslane_02.jpg/220px-Vanguard_at_Faslane_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Vanguard_at_Faslane_02.jpg/330px-Vanguard_at_Faslane_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Vanguard_at_Faslane_02.jpg/440px-Vanguard_at_Faslane_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanguard_at_Faslane_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Vanguard_(S28)" title="HMS Vanguard (S28)">HMS <i>Vanguard</i></a> of the current <a href="/wiki/Vanguard-class_submarine" title="Vanguard-class submarine"><i>Vanguard</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile_submarine" title="Ballistic missile submarine">ballistic missile submarines</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/HMS_Dreadnought_(S101)" title="HMS Dreadnought (S101)">HMS <i>Dreadnought</i></a>, the Royal Navy's first <a href="/wiki/SSN_(hull_classification_symbol)" title="SSN (hull classification symbol)">nuclear submarine</a>, was launched in the 1960s. The navy also received its first nuclear weapons with the introduction of the first of the <a href="/wiki/Resolution-class_submarine" title="Resolution-class submarine"><i>Resolution</i>-class submarines</a> armed with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polaris_missile" title="Polaris missile">Polaris missile</a>. The introduction of Polaris followed the cancellation of the <a href="/wiki/GAM-87_Skybolt" title="GAM-87 Skybolt">GAM-87 Skybolt</a> missile which had been proposed for use by the Air Force's <a href="/wiki/V_bomber" title="V bomber">V bomber</a> force. By the 1990s, the navy became responsible for the maintenance of the UK's entire <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom" title="Nuclear weapons and the United Kingdom">nuclear arsenal</a>. The financial costs attached to nuclear deterrence became an increasingly significant issue for the navy.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Illustrious_at_Speed_MOD_45155641.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2473" data-file-width="1979" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/HMS_Illustrious_at_Speed_MOD_45155641.jpg/170px-HMS_Illustrious_at_Speed_MOD_45155641.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/HMS_Illustrious_at_Speed_MOD_45155641.jpg/255px-HMS_Illustrious_at_Speed_MOD_45155641.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/HMS_Illustrious_at_Speed_MOD_45155641.jpg/340px-HMS_Illustrious_at_Speed_MOD_45155641.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Illustrious_at_Speed_MOD_45155641.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Illustrious_(R06)" title="HMS Illustrious (R06)">HMS <i>Illustrious</i></a>, an <a href="/wiki/Invincible-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Invincible-class aircraft carrier"><i>Invincible</i>-class</a> aircraft carrier</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Navy began plans to replace its fleet of aircraft carriers in the mid-1960s. A plan was drawn up for three large aircraft carriers, each displacing about 60,000 tons; the plan was designated <a href="/wiki/CVA-01" title="CVA-01">CVA-01</a>. These carriers would be able to operate the latest aircraft coming into service and keep the Royal Navy's place as a major naval power.
