The new <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> government that came to power in 1964 was determined to cut defence expenditure as a means to reduce public spending, and in the <a href="/wiki/1966_Defence_White_Paper" title="1966 Defence White Paper">1966 Defence White Paper</a> the project was cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[71]</a></sup> The existing carriers (all built during, or just after World War II) were refitted, two (<a href="/wiki/HMS_Bulwark_(R08)" title="HMS Bulwark (R08)"><i>Bulwark</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Albion_(R07)" title="HMS Albion (R07)"><i>Albion</i></a>) becoming <i>commando</i> carriers, and four (<a href="/wiki/HMS_Victorious_(R38)" title="HMS Victorious (R38)"><i>Victorious</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Eagle_(R05)" title="HMS Eagle (R05)"><i>Eagle</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hermes" title="Hermes">Hermes</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ark_Royal_(R09)" title="HMS Ark Royal (R09)"><i>Ark Royal</i></a>) being completed or rebuilt with modern radars, angled decks, and steam catapults to operate modern jet aircraft<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Starting in 1965 with <a href="/wiki/HMS_Centaur_(R06)" title="HMS Centaur (R06)"><i>Centaur</i></a>, one by one these carriers were decommissioned without replacement, culminating with the 1979 retirement of <i>Ark Royal</i>. By the early 1980s, only <a href="/wiki/HMS_Hermes_(R12)" title="HMS Hermes (R12)"><i>Hermes</i></a> survived and received a refit (just in time for the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>), to operate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_Harriers" title="Sea Harriers">Sea Harriers</a>. She operated along with three much smaller <a href="/wiki/Invincible-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Invincible-class aircraft carrier"><i>Invincible</i>-class</a> aircraft carriers, and the fleet was now centred around anti-submarine warfare in the north Atlantic as opposed to its former position with worldwide strike capability. Along with the war era carriers, all of the war built cruisers and destroyers, along with the post-war built <i>Tiger</i>-class cruisers and large <a href="/wiki/County-class_destroyer" title="County-class destroyer">County-class</a> guided missile destroyers were either retired or sold by 1984.</p>
<p>One of the most important operations conducted predominantly by the Royal Navy after the Second World War was the 1982 defeat of Argentina in the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falkland Islands War</a>. Despite losing four naval ships and other civilian and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Fleet_Auxiliary" title="Royal Fleet Auxiliary">RFA</a> ships, the Royal Navy fought and won a war over 8,000 miles (12,000 km) from Great Britain. <a href="/wiki/HMS_Conqueror_(S48)" title="HMS Conqueror (S48)">HMS <i>Conqueror</i></a> is the only nuclear-powered submarine to have engaged an enemy ship with torpedoes, sinking the cruiser <a href="/wiki/ARA_General_Belgrano" title="ARA General Belgrano">ARA <i>General Belgrano</i></a>. The war also underlined the importance of aircraft carriers and submarines and exposed the weaknesses of the service's late 20th century dependence on chartered merchant vessels.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Albion_MOD_45151289.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/HMS_Albion_MOD_45151289.jpg/220px-HMS_Albion_MOD_45151289.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/HMS_Albion_MOD_45151289.jpg/330px-HMS_Albion_MOD_45151289.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/HMS_Albion_MOD_45151289.jpg/440px-HMS_Albion_MOD_45151289.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Albion_MOD_45151289.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Albion_(L14)" title="HMS Albion (L14)">HMS <i>Albion</i></a>, an <a href="/wiki/Albion-class_landing_platform_dock" title="Albion-class landing platform dock"><i>Albion</i>-class landing platform dock</a> on exercise with the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Marine_Corps" title="Netherlands Marine Corps">Netherlands Marine Corps</a> in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Before the Falklands War, Defence Secretary <a href="/wiki/John_Nott" title="John Nott">John Nott</a> had advocated and initiated a series of cutbacks to the Navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[72]</a></sup> The Falklands War though, provided a reprieve in Nott-proposed cutbacks, and proved a need for the Royal Navy to regain an expeditionary and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Littoral" title="Littoral">littoral</a> capability which, with its resources and structure at the time, would prove difficult. At the beginning of the 1980s, the Royal Navy was a force focused on blue-water anti-submarine warfare. Its purpose was to search for and destroy Soviet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Submarines" title="Submarines">submarines</a> in the North <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_(ocean)" title="Atlantic (ocean)">Atlantic</a>, and to operate the nuclear deterrent submarine force. For a time <i>Hermes</i> was retained, along with all three of the <i>Invincible</i>-class light aircraft carriers. More <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_Harriers" title="Sea Harriers">Sea Harriers</a> were ordered; not just to replace losses, but to also increase the size of the <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Air_Arm" title="Fleet Air Arm">Fleet Air Arm</a>. New and more capable ships were built; notably the <a href="/wiki/Type_42_destroyer" title="Type 42 destroyer"><i>Sheffield</i>-class destroyers</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Type_21_frigate" title="Type 21 frigate">Type 21</a>, <a href="/wiki/Type_22_frigate" title="Type 22 frigate">Type 22</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">Type 23</a> frigates, and new LPDs of the <a href="/wiki/Albion-class_landing_platform_dock" title="Albion-class landing platform dock"><i>Albion</i> class</a>, and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ocean_(L12)" title="HMS Ocean (L12)">HMS <i>Ocean</i></a>, but never in the numbers of the ships that they replaced. As a result, the RN surface fleet continues to reduce in size. A 2013 report found that the current RN was already too small, and that Britain would have to depend on her allies if her territories were attacked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Royal Navy also took part in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kosovo_conflict" title="Kosovo conflict">Kosovo conflict</a>, the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">Afghanistan Campaign</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2003_Iraq_War" title="2003 Iraq War">2003 Iraq War</a>, the last of which saw RN warships <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Gunfire_Support" title="Naval Gunfire Support">bombard</a> positions in support of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Faw_Peninsula" title="Al Faw Peninsula">Al Faw Peninsula</a> landings by Royal Marines. In August 2005, the Royal Navy rescued seven Russians stranded in a submarine off the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka_peninsula" title="Kamchatka peninsula">Kamchatka peninsula</a>. The Navy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scorpio_45" title="Scorpio 45">Scorpio 45</a> remote-controlled mini-sub freed the Russian submarine from the fishing nets and cables that had held it for three days. The Royal Navy was also involved in an <a href="/wiki/Action_of_11_November_2008" title="Action of 11 November 2008">incident involving Somali pirates</a> in November 2008, after the pirates tried to capture a civilian vessel.</p>
<p>The global economic recession of 2008 had a significant impact on the Royal Navy. All <i>Harrier</i> aircraft were retired and put in storage, the carriers <i>Invincible</i> and <i>Ark Royal</i>, as well as the remaining Type-22 frigates were stricken and sold for scrap. <i>Illustrious</i> however, was retained through to 2014 in the <a href="/wiki/Landing_Platform_Helicopter" title="Landing Platform Helicopter">LPH</a> role, until <i>HMS Ocean</i> completed her refit. Plans were made to allow <i>Illustrious</i> to be retained as a floating museum, but by summer of 2016 she too was sold for scrap. <i>Albion</i> and <i>Bulwark</i> rotate in and out of commission as funds are not available to allow both to be active at the same time.</p>
<p>In 2015, the Royal Navy was deployed to the Mediterranean in the <a href="/wiki/EU_Navfor_Med" title="EU Navfor Med">mission</a> to rescue <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_migration_crisis" title="European migration crisis">migrants crossing the Mediterranean</a> from Libya to Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Navy_today">Royal Navy today</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Royal Navy today">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BRNC-Dartmouth.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/BRNC-Dartmouth.jpg/220px-BRNC-Dartmouth.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/BRNC-Dartmouth.jpg/330px-BRNC-Dartmouth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/BRNC-Dartmouth.jpg/440px-BRNC-Dartmouth.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BRNC-Dartmouth.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Britannia Royal Naval College</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/HMS_Raleigh_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Raleigh (shore establishment)">HMS <i>Raleigh</i></a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torpoint,_Cornwall" title="Torpoint, Cornwall">Torpoint, Cornwall</a>, is the basic training facility for newly enlisted personnel. <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Royal_Naval_College" title="Britannia Royal Naval College">Britannia Royal Naval College</a> is the initial officer training establishment for the navy, located at <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth,_Devon" title="Dartmouth, Devon">Dartmouth, Devon</a>. Personnel are divided into a general duties branch, which includes those seamen officers eligible for command, and other branches including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Engineers" title="Royal Naval Engineers">Royal Naval Engineers</a>, medical, and <a href="/wiki/Logistics_Officer" title="Logistics Officer">Logistics Officers</a>, the renamed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supply_Officer" title="Supply Officer">Supply Officer</a> branch. Present day officers and ratings have several different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_uniform" title="Royal Navy uniform">Royal Navy uniforms</a>; some are blue, others are white. Women began to join the Royal Navy in 1917 with the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Royal_Naval_Service" title="Women's Royal Naval Service">Women's Royal Naval Service</a> (WRNS), which was disbanded after the end of the First World War in 1919. It was revived in 1939, and the WRNS continued until disbandment in 1993, as a result of the decision to fully integrate women into the structures of the Royal Navy. The only current restriction on women in the RN is that they may not serve in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a> (they are allowed in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines_Band_Service" title="Royal Marines Band Service">band</a>).</p>
<p>As of 1 January 2015, the Naval Service (Royal Navy and Royal Marines) numbered some 32,880 Regular<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[75]</a></sup> and 3,040 <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="Maritime Reserve (United Kingdom)">Maritime Reserve</a> personnel (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Reserve" title="Royal Naval Reserve">Royal Naval Reserve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines_Reserve" title="Royal Marines Reserve">Royal Marines Reserve</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[76]</a></sup> giving a combined component strength of 35,920 personnel. In addition to the active elements of the Naval Service (Regular and Maritime Reserve), all ex-Regular personnel remain liable to be recalled for duty in <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">a time of need</a>, this is known as the <a href="/wiki/Regular_Reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="Regular Reserve (United Kingdom)">Regular Reserve</a>. In 2002, there were 26,520 Regular Reserves of the Naval Service, of which 13,720 served in the <a href="/wiki/Regular_Reserve_(United_Kingdom)#Royal_Fleet_Reserve" title="Regular Reserve (United Kingdom)">Royal Fleet Reserve</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[77]</a></sup> Publications since April 2013 no-longer report the entire strength of the Regular Reserve, instead they only give a figure for Regular Reserves who serve in the Royal Fleet Reserve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DASA-Reserves-2013_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-DASA-Reserves-2013-83">[78]</a></sup> They had a strength of 7,960 personnel in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DASA-Reserves-2014_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-DASA-Reserves-2014-84">[79]</a></sup> All personnel figures exclude the <a href="/wiki/University_Royal_Naval_Unit" title="University Royal Naval Unit">University Royal Naval Unit</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surface_fleet">Surface fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Surface fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_Royal_Navy_ships" title="List of active Royal Navy ships">List of active Royal Navy ships</a></div>
<dl>
<dt>Large fleet units – amphibious and carriers</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_(R08)_underway_during_trials_with_HMS_Sutherland_(F81)_and_HMS_Iron_Duke_(F234)_on_28_June_2017_(45162784).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_%28R08%29_underway_during_trials_with_HMS_Sutherland_%28F81%29_and_HMS_Iron_Duke_%28F234%29_on_28_June_2017_%2845162784%29.jpg/220px-HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_%28R08%29_underway_during_trials_with_HMS_Sutherland_%28F81%29_and_HMS_Iron_Duke_%28F234%29_on_28_June_2017_%2845162784%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_%28R08%29_underway_during_trials_with_HMS_Sutherland_%28F81%29_and_HMS_Iron_Duke_%28F234%29_on_28_June_2017_%2845162784%29.jpg/330px-HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_%28R08%29_underway_during_trials_with_HMS_Sutherland_%28F81%29_and_HMS_Iron_Duke_%28F234%29_on_28_June_2017_%2845162784%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_%28R08%29_underway_during_trials_with_HMS_Sutherland_%28F81%29_and_HMS_Iron_Duke_%28F234%29_on_28_June_2017_%2845162784%29.jpg/440px-HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_%28R08%29_underway_during_trials_with_HMS_Sutherland_%28F81%29_and_HMS_Iron_Duke_%28F234%29_on_28_June_2017_%2845162784%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_(R08)_underway_during_trials_with_HMS_Sutherland_(F81)_and_HMS_Iron_Duke_(F234)_on_28_June_2017_(45162784).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_(R08)" title="HMS Queen Elizabeth (R08)">HMS <i>Queen Elizabeth</i></a>, a <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Supercarrier" title="Supercarrier">supercarrier</a> on sea trials in June 2017.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The large fleet units in the Royal Navy consisted of <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_warfare_ship" title="Amphibious warfare ship">amphibious warfare ships</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aircraft_carriers" title="Aircraft carriers">aircraft carriers</a>, until August 2014, when the last carrier was decommissioned. Amphibious warfare ships in current service include an <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_assault_ship" title="Amphibious assault ship">amphibious assault ship</a> (<a href="/wiki/HMS_Ocean_(L12)" title="HMS Ocean (L12)">HMS <i>Ocean</i></a>), and two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landing_platform_dock" title="Landing platform dock">landing platform docks</a> (<a href="/wiki/HMS_Albion_(L14)" title="HMS Albion (L14)">HMS <i>Albion</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Bulwark_(L15)" title="HMS Bulwark (L15)">HMS <i>Bulwark</i></a>)—<i>Ocean</i> being the current flagship of the fleet. While their primary role is to conduct amphibious warfare, they have also been deployed for <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">humanitarian aid</a> missions.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/HMS_Illustrious_(R06)" title="HMS Illustrious (R06)">HMS <i>Illustrious</i></a> was the sole remaining aircraft carrier in service with the Royal Navy. Following the retirement of the <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace_Harrier_II" title="British Aerospace Harrier II">Harrier GR9</a> aircraft in 2010, <i>Illustrious</i> had been serving as an amphibious assault ship while <i>Ocean</i> was in refit. <i>Illustrious</i> was decommissioned on 28 August 2014, after <i>Ocean</i> had returned to active duty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[80]</a></sup> However, two much larger <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class aircraft carriers</a> are under construction. These carriers are expected to cost <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>6 billion (double the original estimate),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[81]</a></sup> displace 70,600 tonnes and commence flight trials in 2018. Both are intended to operate the STOVL variant of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-35_Lightning_II" title="F-35 Lightning II">F-35 Lightning II</a>. The first, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_(R08)" title="HMS Queen Elizabeth (R08)">HMS Queen Elizabeth</a> began sea trials in June 2017 and will enter service in 2020, while the second, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Prince_of_Wales_(R09)" title="HMS Prince of Wales (R09)">HMS Prince of Wales</a> will enter service in 2023.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-facts-88">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Navy's large fleet units are supported by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Fleet_Auxiliary" title="Royal Fleet Auxiliary">Royal Fleet Auxiliary</a> which possesses three <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_transport_dock" title="Amphibious transport dock">amphibious transport docks</a> within its operational craft. These are known as the <a href="/wiki/Bay-class_landing_ship" title="Bay-class landing ship"><i>Bay</i>-class</a> landing ships, of which four were introduced in 2006–2007, but one was sold to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Navy" title="Royal Australian Navy">Royal Australian Navy</a> in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[85]</a></sup> In November 2006, the <a href="/wiki/First_Sea_Lord" title="First Sea Lord">First Sea Lord</a> Admiral Sir <a href="/wiki/Jonathon_Band" title="Jonathon Band">Jonathon Band</a> described the Royal Fleet Auxiliary vessels as "a major uplift in the Royal Navy's war fighting capability."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[86]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Major surface combatants – destroyers and frigates</dt>
</dl>
<p>The escort fleet, in the form of <a href="/wiki/Guided_missile_destroyer" title="Guided missile destroyer">guided missile destroyers</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frigates" title="Frigates">frigates</a>, is the traditional workhorse of the Navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MODRNinfo_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-MODRNinfo-92">[87]</a></sup> As of January 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there are six <a href="/wiki/Type_45_destroyer" title="Type 45 destroyer">Type 45 destroyers</a> and 13 <a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">Type 23 frigates</a> in active service. Among their primary roles is to provide escort for the larger capital ships—protecting them from air, surface and subsurface threats. Other duties include undertaking the Royal Navy's <a href="/wiki/Standing_Royal_Navy_deployments" title="Standing Royal Navy deployments">standing deployments</a> across the globe, which often consists of: counter-narcotics, anti-piracy missions and providing humanitarian aid.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Duncan_(7899777334).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Duncan_%287899777334%29.jpg/220px-Duncan_%287899777334%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Duncan_%287899777334%29.jpg/330px-Duncan_%287899777334%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Duncan_%287899777334%29.jpg/440px-Duncan_%287899777334%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Duncan_(7899777334).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Duncan_(D37)" title="HMS Duncan (D37)">HMS <i>Duncan</i></a>, the last <a href="/wiki/Type_45_destroyer" title="Type 45 destroyer">Type 45</a> <a href="/wiki/Guided_missile_destroyer" title="Guided missile destroyer">guided missile destroyer</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All six Type 45 destroyers have been built and are in commission, with <a href="/wiki/HMS_Duncan_(D37)" title="HMS Duncan (D37)">HMS <i>Duncan</i></a> being the last and final Type 45 entering service in September 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[88]</a></sup> The new Type 45 destroyers replaced the older <a href="/wiki/Type_42_destroyer" title="Type 42 destroyer">Type 42 destroyers</a>. The Type 45 is primarily designed for <a href="/wiki/Anti-aircraft_warfare" title="Anti-aircraft warfare">anti-aircraft and anti-missile warfare</a> and the Royal Navy describe the destroyers mission as "to shield the Fleet from air attack".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[89]</a></sup> They are equipped with the <a href="/wiki/PAAMS" title="PAAMS">PAAMS</a> (also known as Sea Viper) integrated anti-aircraft warfare system which incorporates the sophisticated <a href="/wiki/SAMPSON" title="SAMPSON">SAMPSON</a> and <a href="/wiki/S1850M" title="S1850M">S1850M</a> long range radars and the <a href="/wiki/Aster_(missile_family)" title="Aster (missile family)">Aster 15 and 30</a> missiles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAEType45_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-BAEType45-95">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially, 16 Type 23 frigates were delivered to the Royal Navy, with the final vessel, <a href="/wiki/HMS_St_Albans_(F83)" title="HMS St Albans (F83)">HMS <i>St Albans</i></a>, commissioned in June 2002. However, the 2004 review of defence spending (<a href="/wiki/Delivering_Security_in_a_Changing_World" title="Delivering Security in a Changing World">Delivering Security in a Changing World</a>) announced that three frigates of the fleet of sixteen would be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paid_off" title="Paid off">paid off</a> as part of a continuous cost-cutting strategy, and these were subsequently sold to the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Navy" title="Chilean Navy">Chilean Navy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SellType23_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-SellType23-96">[91]</a></sup> The 2010 <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Defence_and_Security_Review_2010" title="Strategic Defence and Security Review 2010">Strategic Defence and Security Review</a> announced that the remaining 13 Type 23 frigates would eventually be replaced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_Combat_Ship" title="Global Combat Ship">Global Combat Ship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[92]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Mine countermeasure, patrol and survey vessels</dt>
</dl>
<p>At the beginning of the 1990s, the Royal Navy had two classes of offshore patrol vessel, the <a href="/wiki/Island-class_patrol_vessel" title="Island-class patrol vessel"><i>Island</i>-class</a>, and the larger <a href="/wiki/Castle-class_patrol_vessel" title="Castle-class patrol vessel"><i>Castle</i>-class</a>. However, in 1997, a decision was taken to replace them; this decision came in the form of three much larger offshore patrol vessels, the <a href="/wiki/River-class_patrol_vessel" title="River-class patrol vessel"><i>River</i>-class</a>. Unusually, the three River-class ships were owned by <a href="/wiki/VT_Group" title="VT Group">Vosper Thorneycroft</a>, and leased to the Royal Navy until 2013. This relationship was defined by a ground-breaking contractor logistic support contract which contracts the ships' availability to the RN, including technical and stores support. A modified River-class vessel, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Clyde_(P257)" title="HMS Clyde (P257)">HMS <i>Clyde</i></a>, was commissioned in July 2007 and became the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> guard-ship. In November 2013, it was announced that in order to sustain shipbuilding capabilities on the Clyde, five new ocean-going patrol vessels with <a href="/wiki/AgustaWestland_AW101" title="AgustaWestland AW101">Merlin-capable</a> flightdecks would be ordered for delivery from 2017. These ships will replace the four existing River Class ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[93]</a></sup> In October 2014, the Ministry of Defence announced the names of the first three ships as <a href="/wiki/HMS_Forth_(P222)" title="HMS Forth (P222)">HMS <i>Forth</i></a>, HMS <i>Medway</i> and HMS <i>Trent</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[94]</a></sup> The fourth and fifth ships were ordered in December 2016, these will be named HMS <i>Spey</i> and HMS <i>Tamar</i> respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[95]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Protector_Assisting_the_Antarctic_Community._MOD_45156397.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/HMS_Protector_Assisting_the_Antarctic_Community._MOD_45156397.jpg/220px-HMS_Protector_Assisting_the_Antarctic_Community._MOD_45156397.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/HMS_Protector_Assisting_the_Antarctic_Community._MOD_45156397.jpg/330px-HMS_Protector_Assisting_the_Antarctic_Community._MOD_45156397.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/HMS_Protector_Assisting_the_Antarctic_Community._MOD_45156397.jpg/440px-HMS_Protector_Assisting_the_Antarctic_Community._MOD_45156397.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Protector_Assisting_the_Antarctic_Community._MOD_45156397.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Protector_(A173)" title="HMS Protector (A173)">HMS <i>Protector</i></a>, a Royal Navy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Antarctica" title="British Antarctica">Antarctic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patrol_ship" title="Patrol ship">patrol ship</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Royal Navy's largest patrol ship is <a href="/wiki/HMS_Protector_(A173)" title="HMS Protector (A173)">HMS <i>Protector</i></a>. <i>Protector</i> is a dedicated Antarctic patrol ship that fulfils the nations mandate to provide support to the <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Survey" title="British Antarctic Survey">British Antarctic Survey</a> (BAS).</p>
<p>Mine countermeasure vessels in service with the Royal Navy include: seven <a href="/wiki/Sandown-class_minehunter" title="Sandown-class minehunter"><i>Sandown</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Minehunter" title="Minehunter">minehunters</a> and eight <a href="/wiki/Hunt-class_mine_countermeasures_vessel" title="Hunt-class mine countermeasures vessel"><i>Hunt</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Mine_countermeasures_vessel" title="Mine countermeasures vessel">mine countermeasure vessels</a>. The <i>Hunt</i>-class combine the separate roles of the traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minesweeper_(ship)" title="Minesweeper (ship)">minesweeper</a> and the active minehunter in one hull. If required, the <i>Sandown</i> and <i>Hunt</i>-class vessels can take on the role of offshore patrol vessels. <a href="/wiki/HMS_Scott_(H131)" title="HMS Scott (H131)">HMS <i>Scott</i></a> is an ocean survey vessel and at 13,500 tonnes is one of the largest ships in the Navy. The other survey vessels of the Royal Navy are the two multi-role ships of the <a href="/wiki/Echo-class_survey_ship_(2002)" title="Echo-class survey ship (2002)"><i>Echo</i>-class</a>, which came into service in 2002 and 2003, and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Gleaner_(H86)" title="HMS Gleaner (H86)">HMS <i>Gleaner</i></a>, which at just over 20 tonnes is the smallest commissioned vessel in the Navy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Submarine_Service">Submarine Service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Submarine Service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_Submarine_Service" title="Royal Navy Submarine Service">Royal Navy Submarine Service</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Astute_Arrives_at_Faslane_for_the_First_Time_MOD_45150806.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/HMS_Astute_Arrives_at_Faslane_for_the_First_Time_MOD_45150806.jpg/220px-HMS_Astute_Arrives_at_Faslane_for_the_First_Time_MOD_45150806.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/HMS_Astute_Arrives_at_Faslane_for_the_First_Time_MOD_45150806.jpg/330px-HMS_Astute_Arrives_at_Faslane_for_the_First_Time_MOD_45150806.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/HMS_Astute_Arrives_at_Faslane_for_the_First_Time_MOD_45150806.jpg/440px-HMS_Astute_Arrives_at_Faslane_for_the_First_Time_MOD_45150806.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Astute_Arrives_at_Faslane_for_the_First_Time_MOD_45150806.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMS_Astute_(S119)" title="HMS Astute (S119)">HMS <i>Astute</i></a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Astute-class_submarine" title="Astute-class submarine"><i>Astute</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarine" title="Nuclear submarine">nuclear submarine</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Submarine Service is the <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a> based element of the Royal Navy. It is sometimes referred to as the "<i>Silent Service</i>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[96]</a></sup> as the submarines are generally required to operate undetected. The service was founded in 1901. The service made history in 1982 when, during the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Conqueror_(S48)" title="HMS Conqueror (S48)">HMS <i>Conqueror</i></a> became the first nuclear-powered submarine to sink a surface ship, the <a href="/wiki/ARA_General_Belgrano" title="ARA General Belgrano">ARA <i>General Belgrano</i></a>. Today, the Submarine Service consists of <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile_submarine" title="Ballistic missile submarine">ballistic missile submarines</a> (SSBN) and <a href="/wiki/SSN_(hull_classification_symbol)" title="SSN (hull classification symbol)">fleet submarines</a> (SSN). All of the Royal Navy's submarines are <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_marine_propulsion" title="Nuclear marine propulsion">nuclear-powered</a>.</p>
<p>Of ballistic missile submarines, the Royal Navy operates the four <a href="/wiki/Vanguard-class_submarine" title="Vanguard-class submarine"><i>Vanguard</i>-class</a>, each displacing nearly 16,000 tonnes and equipped with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trident_Missile" title="Trident Missile">Trident II</a> missiles (armed with <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom" title="Nuclear weapons and the United Kingdom">nuclear weapons</a>) and heavyweight <a href="/wiki/Spearfish_torpedo" title="Spearfish torpedo">Spearfish torpedoes</a>, with the purpose to carry out Operation Relentless, the United Kingdom's Continuous At Sea Deterrent (Abbreviated to CASD). In December 2006, the Government published recommendations for a new class of four ballistic missile submarines to replace the current <i>Vanguard</i>-class, starting 2024. These new <a href="/wiki/Dreadnought-class_submarine" title="Dreadnought-class submarine"><i>Dreadnought</i>-class submarines</a> will mean that the United Kingdom will maintain a nuclear ballistic missile submarine fleet and the ability to launch nuclear weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Six fleet submarines are presently in service, with three <a href="/wiki/Trafalgar-class_submarine" title="Trafalgar-class submarine"><i>Trafalgar</i>-class</a> and three <a href="/wiki/Astute-class_submarine" title="Astute-class submarine"><i>Astute</i>-class</a> (with the remainder in construction) making up the total. The <i>Trafalgar</i>-class displace little over 5,300 tonnes when submerged and are armed with <a href="/wiki/Tomahawk_(missile)" title="Tomahawk (missile)">Tomahawk</a> land-attack missiles and Spearfish torpedoes. The <i>Astute</i>-class at 7,400 tonnes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[98]</a></sup> are much larger and carry a larger number of Tomahawk missiles and Spearfish torpedoes. Four more <i>Astute</i>-class fleet submarines are expected to be commissioned and will eventually replace the remaining <i>Trafalgar</i>-class boats. <a href="/wiki/HMS_Artful_(S121)" title="HMS Artful (S121)">HMS <i>Artful</i></a> was the latest <i>Astute</i>-class boat to be commissioned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commissioning_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Commissioning-104">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2010 Strategic Defence and Security Review, the UK Government reaffirmed its intention to procure seven <i>Astute</i>-class submarines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-direct.gov.uk_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-direct.gov.uk-105">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet_Air_Arm">Fleet Air Arm</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Fleet Air Arm">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Air_Arm" title="Fleet Air Arm">Fleet Air Arm</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UK_F-35B_Lightning_II_MOD_45157752.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2095" data-file-width="3364" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/UK_F-35B_Lightning_II_MOD_45157752.jpg/220px-UK_F-35B_Lightning_II_MOD_45157752.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/UK_F-35B_Lightning_II_MOD_45157752.jpg/330px-UK_F-35B_Lightning_II_MOD_45157752.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/UK_F-35B_Lightning_II_MOD_45157752.jpg/440px-UK_F-35B_Lightning_II_MOD_45157752.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UK_F-35B_Lightning_II_MOD_45157752.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-35_Lightning_II" title="F-35 Lightning II">F-35B</a> will be operated from the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class aircraft carriers</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Fleet Air Arm (FAA) is the branch of the Royal Navy responsible for the operation of naval aircraft, it can trace its roots back to 1912 and the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Flying_Corps" title="Royal Flying Corps">Royal Flying Corps</a>. The Fleet Air Arm currently operates helicopters: the <a href="/wiki/AgustaWestland_AW101" title="AgustaWestland AW101">AgustaWestland Merlin</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AgustaWestland_AW159" title="AgustaWestland AW159">AgustaWestland Wildcat</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Westland_Sea_King" title="Westland Sea King">Westland Sea King</a>. The primary role of these helicopters is to conduct <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare" title="Anti-submarine warfare">anti-submarine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anti-surface_warfare" title="Anti-surface warfare">anti-surface warfare</a> as well as reconnaissance, medium-lift, troop-transport and <a href="/wiki/Airborne_early_warning_and_control" title="Airborne early warning and control">airborne early warning and control</a> missions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Pilots designated for rotary wing service train at the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Helicopter_Flying_School" title="Defence Helicopter Flying School">Defence Helicopter Flying School</a> at RAF Shawbury.</p>
<p>With the retirement of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Force_Harrier" title="Joint Force Harrier">Joint Force Harrier</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BAE_Harrier_II" title="BAE Harrier II">Harrier GR7/GR9</a> strike aircraft in 2010, the FAA has no fixed-wing aircraft in front-line operations. There is an intention to operate the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_F-35_Lightning_II" title="Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning II">Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning II</a> B version with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>. <a href="/wiki/809_Naval_Air_Squadron" title="809 Naval Air Squadron">809 NAS</a> is hoped to be the first FAA Squadron to operate that aircraft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[101]</a></sup> The F-35B will be operated from the Navy's new <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class aircraft carriers</a> starting 2018 for initial flight training. For information regarding the types of aircraft operated by the Fleet Air Arm, see <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_active_United_Kingdom_military_aircraft" title="List of active United Kingdom military aircraft">List of active United Kingdom military aircraft</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Marines">Royal Marines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Royal Marines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Marines_in_Sangin_MOD_45151554.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Royal_Marines_in_Sangin_MOD_45151554.jpg/220px-Royal_Marines_in_Sangin_MOD_45151554.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Royal_Marines_in_Sangin_MOD_45151554.jpg/330px-Royal_Marines_in_Sangin_MOD_45151554.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Royal_Marines_in_Sangin_MOD_45151554.jpg/440px-Royal_Marines_in_Sangin_MOD_45151554.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Marines_in_Sangin_MOD_45151554.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a> in Sangin, 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Royal Marines are an amphibious, specialised <a href="/wiki/Light_infantry" title="Light infantry">light infantry</a> force of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commandos" title="Commandos">commandos</a>, capable of deploying at short notice in support of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Government" title="Her Majesty's Government">Her Majesty's Government</a>'s military and diplomatic objectives overseas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[102]</a></sup> The Royal Marines are organised into a highly mobile light infantry brigade (<a href="/wiki/3_Commando_Brigade" title="3 Commando Brigade">3 Commando Brigade</a>) and a number of separate units, including <a href="/wiki/1_Assault_Group_Royal_Marines" title="1 Assault Group Royal Marines">1 Assault Group Royal Marines</a>, <a href="/wiki/43_Commando_Fleet_Protection_Group_Royal_Marines" title="43 Commando Fleet Protection Group Royal Marines">43 Commando Fleet Protection Group Royal Marines</a> and a company strength commitment to the <a href="/wiki/Special_Forces_Support_Group" title="Special Forces Support Group">Special Forces Support Group</a>. The Corps operates in all environments and climates, though particular expertise and training is spent on <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_warfare" title="Amphibious warfare">amphibious warfare</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctic_warfare" title="Arctic warfare">Arctic warfare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_warfare" title="Mountain warfare">mountain warfare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expeditionary_warfare" title="Expeditionary warfare">expeditionary warfare</a> and commitment to the UK's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_Reaction_Force" title="Rapid Reaction Force">Rapid Reaction</a> Force. The Royal Marines also primarily arm the <a href="/wiki/Special_Boat_Service" title="Special Boat Service">Special Boat Service</a> (SBS), the waterborne section of the UK's Elite Special Forces</p>
<p>The Royal Marines have seen action in a number of wars, often fighting beside the British Army; including in the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, the Napoleonic Wars, the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>, World War I and World War II. In recent times, the Corps has been deployed in expeditionary warfare roles, such as the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="Sierra Leone Civil War">Sierra Leone Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">War in Afghanistan</a>. The Royal Marines have international ties with allied marine forces, particularly the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod.uk_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod.uk-108">[103]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Marine_Corps" title="Netherlands Marine Corps">Netherlands Marine Corps</a>/Korps Mariniers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-royalnavy.mod.uk_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-royalnavy.mod.uk-109">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_bases">Naval bases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Naval bases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Albion_2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="1840" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/HMS_Albion_2006.jpg/220px-HMS_Albion_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/HMS_Albion_2006.jpg/330px-HMS_Albion_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/HMS_Albion_2006.jpg/440px-HMS_Albion_2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Albion_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/HMS_Albion_(L14)" title="HMS Albion (L14)">HMS Albion</a> during the <i>HMNB Devonport Navy days 2006</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Royal Navy currently uses 3 major naval bases in the UK, each housing its own flotilla of ships and boats ready for service. The RN also uses and has property in Bahrain, as the Naval Support Center in Manama.</p>
<ul>
<li>HMNB Devonport (HMS Drake) - Currently the largest operational naval base in Western Europe, Devonport's flotilla consists of the RN's three amphibious assault carriers (HMS Ocean, HMS Bulwark, HMS Albion), a large fleet of <a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">Duke-Class Frigates</a> (Type 23). Also, Devonport homes some of the RN's Submarines service, including the fleet of <a href="/wiki/Trafalgar-class_submarine" title="Trafalgar-class submarine">Trafalgar Class Submarines</a>.</li>
<li>HMNB Portsmouth (HMS Portsmouth) - Home to the future Queen Elizabeth Class supercarriers, Portsmouth is also the home to the Daring Class Stealth Destroyers (commonly known as Type 45) as well as mine-clearance vessels, and a moderate fleet of Type 23 frigates as well as Fishery Protection Squadrons.</li>
<li>HMNB Clyde (HMS Neptune Or Simply 'Faslane') - Situated in Central Scotland along the Clyde River, Faslane is known as the home of the UK's nuclear deterrent, as it maintains the fleet of Vanguard Class Ballistic Missile Submarines, as well as the fleet of Astute Class Fleet (Hunter-Killer) submarines. By 2020, Faslane will become the home to all Royal Navy submarines, and thus the RN Submarine Service. As a result, 43 Commando (Fleet Protection Group) are stationed in Faslane alongside to guard the base as well as The Royal Naval Armaments Depot at Coulport. Moreover, Faslane also operates a medium-sized fleet of patrol vessels.
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Vigilant_alongside_Faslane_Naval_Base._MOD_45147682.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2357" data-file-width="3000" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/HMS_Vigilant_alongside_Faslane_Naval_Base._MOD_45147682.jpg/220px-HMS_Vigilant_alongside_Faslane_Naval_Base._MOD_45147682.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/HMS_Vigilant_alongside_Faslane_Naval_Base._MOD_45147682.jpg/330px-HMS_Vigilant_alongside_Faslane_Naval_Base._MOD_45147682.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/HMS_Vigilant_alongside_Faslane_Naval_Base._MOD_45147682.jpg/440px-HMS_Vigilant_alongside_Faslane_Naval_Base._MOD_45147682.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Vigilant_alongside_Faslane_Naval_Base._MOD_45147682.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
HMS Vigilant alongside Faslane Naval Base</div>
</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1685" data-file-width="2570" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg/220px-Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg/330px-Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg/440px-Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Royal Navy <a href="/wiki/AgustaWestland_AW101" title="AgustaWestland AW101">EH-101 Merlin</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RIAT" title="RIAT">RIAT</a> 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The current role of the Royal Navy is to protect British interests at home and abroad, executing the foreign and defence policies of Her Majesty's Government through the exercise of military effect, diplomatic activities and other activities in support of these objectives. The Royal Navy is also a key element of the British contribution to NATO, with a number of assets allocated to NATO tasks at any time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[105]</a></sup> These objectives are delivered via a number of core capabilities:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[106]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Maintenance of the UK Nuclear Deterrent through a policy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanguard_class_submarine" title="Vanguard class submarine"><i>Continuous at Sea Deterrence</i></a>.</li>
<li>Provision of two medium scale <a href="/wiki/Carrier_battle_group" title="Carrier battle group">maritime task groups</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Air_Arm" title="Fleet Air Arm">Fleet Air Arm</a>.</li>
<li>Delivery of the UK <a href="/wiki/British_Commandos" title="British Commandos">Commando</a> force.</li>
<li>Contribution of assets to the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Helicopter_Command" title="Joint Helicopter Command">Joint Helicopter Command</a>.</li>
<li>Maintenance of <a href="/wiki/Standing_Royal_Navy_deployments" title="Standing Royal Navy deployments">standing patrol commitments</a>.</li>
<li>Provision of <a href="/wiki/Minehunter" title="Minehunter">mine counter measures</a> capability to United Kingdom and allied commitments.</li>
<li>Provision of <a href="/wiki/Hydrography" title="Hydrography">hydrographic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meteorological" title="Meteorological">meteorological</a> services deployable worldwide.</li>
<li>Protection of Britain and EU's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_deployments">Current deployments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Current deployments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Standing_Royal_Navy_deployments" title="Standing Royal Navy deployments">Standing Royal Navy deployments</a></div>
<p>The Royal Navy is currently deployed in different areas of the world, including some <a href="/wiki/Standing_Royal_Navy_deployments" title="Standing Royal Navy deployments">standing Royal Navy deployments</a>. These include several home tasks as well as overseas deployments. The Navy is deployed in the Mediterranean as part of standing NATO deployments including mine countermeasures and NATO Maritime Group 2. In both the North and South Atlantic RN vessels are patrolling. There is always a Falkland Islands patrol vessel on deployment, currently <a href="/wiki/HMS_Clyde_(P257)" title="HMS Clyde (P257)">HMS <i>Clyde</i></a>.</p>
<p>The Royal Navy operates a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Response_Force_Task_Group" title="Response Force Task Group">Response Force Task Group</a> (a product of the 2010 Strategic Defence and Security Review), which is poised to respond globally to short-notice tasking across a range of defence activities, such as non-combatant evacuation operations, disaster relief, humanitarian aid or amphibious operations. In 2011, the first deployment of the task group occurred under the name 'COUGAR 11' which saw them transit through the Mediterranean where they took part in multinational amphibious exercises before moving further east through the Suez Canal for further exercises in the Indian Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[108]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1912" data-file-width="3000" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg/220px-RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg/330px-RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg/440px-RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The RN presence in the Persian Gulf typically consists of a Type 45 destroyer and a squadron of minehunters supported by an RFA <a href="/wiki/Bay-class_landing_ship" title="Bay-class landing ship">Bay-class</a> "mothership"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, the RN sustains commitments in support of both national and coalition efforts to stabilise the region. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armilla_Patrol" title="Armilla Patrol">Armilla Patrol</a>, which started in 1980, is the navy's primary commitment the Gulf region. The Royal Navy also contributes to the combined maritime forces in the Gulf in support of coalition operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[109]</a></sup> The UK Maritime Component Commander, overseer of all of Her Majesty's warships in the Persian Gulf and surrounding waters, is also deputy commander of the Combined Maritime Forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[110]</a></sup> The Royal Navy has been responsible for training the fledgling <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Navy" title="Iraqi Navy">Iraqi Navy</a> and securing Iraq's oil terminals following the cessation of hostilities in the country. The Iraqi Training and Advisory Mission (Navy) (Umm Qasr), headed by a Royal Navy captain, has been responsible for the former duty whilst Commander Task Force Iraqi Maritime, a Royal Navy commodore, has been responsible for the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Royal Navy contributes to standing NATO formations and maintains forces as part of the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Response_Force" title="NATO Response Force">NATO Response Force</a>. The RN also has a long-standing commitment to supporting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five_Powers_Defence_Arrangements" title="Five Powers Defence Arrangements">Five Powers Defence Arrangements</a> countries and occasionally deploys to the Far East as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[113]</a></sup> This deployment typically consists of a <a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">frigate</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Echo-class_survey_ship_(2002)" title="Echo-class survey ship (2002)">survey vessel</a>, operating separately. <a href="/wiki/Operation_Atalanta" title="Operation Atalanta">Operation Atalanta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s anti-<a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a> operation in the Indian Ocean, is permanently commanded by a senior Royal Navy or Royal Marines officer at <a href="/wiki/Northwood_Headquarters" title="Northwood Headquarters">Northwood Headquarters</a> and the navy contributes ships to the operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="Command,_control_and_organisation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Command.2C_control_and_organisation">Command, control and organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Command, control and organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The titular head of the Royal Navy is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_High_Admiral_(United_Kingdom)" title="Lord High Admiral (United Kingdom)">Lord High Admiral</a>, a position which has been held by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">the Duke of Edinburgh</a> since 2011. The position had been held by Queen Elizabeth II from 1964 to 2011;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[115]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">Sovereign</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief_of_the_British_Armed_Forces" title="Commander-in-chief of the British Armed Forces">Commander-in-chief of the British Armed Forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[116]</a></sup> The professional head of the Naval Service is the <a href="/wiki/First_Sea_Lord" title="First Sea Lord">First Sea Lord</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Admiral_(United_Kingdom)" title="Admiral (United Kingdom)">admiral</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Defence Council of the United Kingdom">Defence Council of the United Kingdom</a>. The Defence Council delegates management of the Naval Service to the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Board_(United_Kingdom)" title="Admiralty Board (United Kingdom)">Admiralty Board</a>, chaired by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Defence" title="Secretary of State for Defence">Secretary of State for Defence</a>, which directs the <a href="/wiki/Navy_Board" title="Navy Board">Navy Board</a>, a sub-committee of the Admiralty Board comprising only naval officers and <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> (MOD) civil servants. These are all based in <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)#Property_portfolio" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">MOD Main Building</a> in London, where the First Sea Lord, also known as the Chief of the Naval Staff, is supported by the Naval Staff Department.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation">Organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Commander" title="Fleet Commander">Fleet Commander</a> has responsibility for the provision of ships, submarines and aircraft ready for any operations that the Government requires. Fleet Commander exercises his authority through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navy_Command_Headquarters" title="Navy Command Headquarters">Navy Command Headquarters</a>, based at <a href="/wiki/HMS_Excellent_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Excellent (shore establishment)">HMS <i>Excellent</i></a> in Portsmouth. An operational headquarters, the <a href="/wiki/Northwood_Headquarters" title="Northwood Headquarters">Northwood Headquarters</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Northwood,_London" title="Northwood, London">Northwood</a>, London, is co-located with the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Joint_Headquarters" title="Permanent Joint Headquarters">Permanent Joint Headquarters</a> of the United Kingdom's armed forces, and a NATO Regional Command, Allied Maritime Component Command Northwood.</p>
<p>The Royal Navy was the first of the three armed forces to combine the personnel and training command, under the Principal Personnel Officer, with the operational and policy command, combining the Headquarters of the Commander-in-Chief, Fleet and Naval Home Command into a single organisation, Fleet Command, in 2005 and becoming Navy Command in 2008. Within the combined command, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sea_Lord" title="Second Sea Lord">Second Sea Lord</a> continues to act as the Principal Personnel Officer.</p>
<p>The Naval Command senior appointments are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[117]</a></sup></p>

<p>Intelligence support to fleet operations is provided by intelligence sections at the various headquarters and from MOD <a href="/wiki/Defence_Intelligence" title="Defence Intelligence">Defence Intelligence</a>, renamed from the Defence Intelligence Staff in early 2010. There are further details of the Royal Navy's historical organisation at <a href="/wiki/List_of_fleets_and_major_commands_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="List of fleets and major commands of the Royal Navy">List of fleets and major commands of the Royal Navy</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">Locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg/220px-International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg/330px-International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg/440px-International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a> dockyard during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trafalgar_200" title="Trafalgar 200">Trafalgar 200</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Fleet_Review" title="International Fleet Review">International Fleet Review</a>. Seen here are commissioned ships from; the United Kingdom, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMNB_Clyde.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="792" data-file-width="640" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/HMNB_Clyde.jpg/170px-HMNB_Clyde.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/HMNB_Clyde.jpg/255px-HMNB_Clyde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/HMNB_Clyde.jpg/340px-HMNB_Clyde.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMNB_Clyde.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMNB_Clyde" title="HMNB Clyde">HMNB Clyde</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faslane" title="Faslane">Faslane</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Vanguard-class_submarine" title="Vanguard-class submarine"><i>Vanguard</i>-class</a> submarines</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Royal_Navy_shore_establishments" title="List of Royal Navy shore establishments">List of Royal Navy shore establishments</a></div>
<p>The Royal Navy currently operates from three bases in the United Kingdom where commissioned ships are based; <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Portsmouth" title="HMNB Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Clyde" title="HMNB Clyde">Clyde</a> and <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">Devonport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> – Devonport is the largest operational naval base in the UK and Western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[118]</a></sup> Each base hosts a flotilla command under a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commodore_(RN)" title="Commodore (RN)">commodore</a>, or, in the case of Clyde, a captain, responsible for the provision of operational capability using the ships and submarines within the flotilla. <a href="/wiki/3_Commando_Brigade" title="3 Commando Brigade">3 Commando Brigade</a> Royal Marines is similarly commanded by a <a href="/wiki/Brigadier" title="Brigadier">brigadier</a> and based in Plymouth. Historically, the Royal Navy maintained <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_Dockyards" title="Royal Navy Dockyards">Royal Navy Dockyards</a> around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[119]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dockyard" title="Dockyard">Dockyards</a> of the Royal Navy are harbours where ships are overhauled and refitted. Only four are operating today; at Devonport, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faslane_Naval_Base" title="Faslane Naval Base">Faslane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosyth_Dockyard" title="Rosyth Dockyard">Rosyth</a> and at Portsmouth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKNDABlackham_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKNDABlackham-125">[120]</a></sup> A Naval Base Review was undertaken in 2006 and early 2007, the outcome being announced by Secretary of State for Defence, <a href="/wiki/Des_Browne" title="Des Browne">Des Browne</a>, confirming that all would remain however some reductions in manpower were anticipated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>The academy where initial training for future Royal Navy officers takes place is Britannia Royal Naval College, located on a hill overlooking <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth,_Devon" title="Dartmouth, Devon">Dartmouth, Devon</a>. Basic training for future <a href="/wiki/Naval_rating" title="Naval rating">ratings</a> takes place at <a href="/wiki/HMS_Raleigh_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Raleigh (shore establishment)">HMS <i>Raleigh</i></a> at <a href="/wiki/Torpoint" title="Torpoint">Torpoint</a>, Cornwall, close to HMNB Devonport.</p>
<p>Significant numbers of naval personnel are employed within the Ministry of Defence, Defence Equipment and Support and on exchange with the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>. Small numbers are also on exchange within other government departments and with allied fleets, such as the United States Navy. The navy also posts personnel in small units around the world to support ongoing operations and maintain standing commitments. Nineteen personnel are stationed in Gibraltar to support the small <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Squadron" title="Gibraltar Squadron">Gibraltar Squadron</a>, the RN's only permanent overseas squadron. A number of personnel are also based at East Cove Military Port and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Mount_Pleasant" title="RAF Mount Pleasant">RAF Mount Pleasant</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> to support APT(S). Small numbers of personnel are based in <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a> (Naval Party 1002), Miami (NP 1011 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AUTEC" title="AUTEC">AUTEC</a>), Singapore (NP 1022), <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> (NP 1023) and elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 December 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">Foreign and Commonwealth Office</a> announced it would expand the UK's naval facilities in <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> to support larger Royal Navy ships deployed to the Persian Gulf. Once complete, it will be the UK's first permanent military base located <a href="/wiki/East_of_Suez" title="East of Suez">East of Suez</a> since it withdrew from the region in 1971. The base will reportedly be large enough to accommodate <a href="/wiki/Type_45_destroyer" title="Type 45 destroyer">Type 45</a> destroyers and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class</a> aircraft carriers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_and_naming">Titles and naming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Titles and naming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2514" data-file-width="1947" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg/170px-HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg/255px-HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg/340px-HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">Type 23 frigates</a> or "Duke class" are named after <a href="/wiki/Duke#United_Kingdom" title="Duke">British dukes</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Of_the_Navy">Of the Navy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Of the Navy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The navy of the United Kingdom is commonly referred to as the "Royal Navy" both in the United Kingdom and other countries. Navies of other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> countries <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">where the British monarch is also head of state</a> include their national name, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Navy" title="Royal Australian Navy">Royal Australian Navy</a>. Some navies of other monarchies, such as the <i>Koninklijke Marine</i> (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Navy" title="Royal Netherlands Navy">Royal Netherlands Navy</a>) and <i>Kungliga Flottan</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Navy" title="Royal Swedish Navy">Royal Swedish Navy</a>), are also called "Royal Navy" in their own language. The Danish Navy stands out with the term Royal incorporated in its official name (Royal Danish Navy), but only using the term "Flåden" (Navy) in everyday speech.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[126]</a></sup> The French Navy, despite France being a republic since 1870, is often nicknamed <i>"La Royale"</i> (literally: The Royal).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Of_ships">Of ships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Of ships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_ships_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="List of ships of the Royal Navy">List of ships of the Royal Navy</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_Royal_Navy_ships" title="List of active Royal Navy ships">List of active Royal Navy ships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naming_conventions_for_destroyers_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="Naming conventions for destroyers of the Royal Navy">Naming conventions for destroyers of the Royal Navy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Type_system_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="Type system of the Royal Navy">Type system of the Royal Navy</a></div>
<p>Royal Navy ships in commission are prefixed since 1789 with <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Ship" title="Her Majesty's Ship">Her Majesty's Ship</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/His_Majesty%27s_Ship" title="His Majesty's Ship">His Majesty's Ship</a>), abbreviated to "HMS"; for example, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Beagle" title="HMS Beagle">HMS <i>Beagle</i></a>. Submarines are styled HM Submarine, also abbreviated "HMS". Names are allocated to ships and submarines by a naming committee within the MOD and given by class, with the names of ships within a class often being thematic (for example, the <a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">Type 23s</a> are named after <a href="/wiki/Duke#United_Kingdom" title="Duke">British dukes</a>) or traditional (for example, the <a href="/wiki/Invincible-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Invincible-class aircraft carrier"><i>Invincible</i>-class aircraft carriers</a> all carry the names of famous historic ships). Names are frequently re-used, offering a new ship the rich heritage, battle honours and traditions of her predecessors. Often, a particular vessel class will be named after the first ship of that type to be built.</p>
<p>As well as a name, each ship and submarine of the Royal Navy and the Royal Fleet Auxiliary is given a <a href="/wiki/Pennant_number" title="Pennant number">pennant number</a> which in part denotes its role. For example, the destroyer <a href="/wiki/HMS_Daring_(D32)" title="HMS Daring (D32)">HMS <i>Daring</i></a> displays the pennant number 'D32'.</p>
<h2><span id="Ranks,_rates_and_insignia"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranks.2C_rates_and_insignia">Ranks, rates and insignia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ranks, rates and insignia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_uniform" title="Royal Navy uniform">Royal Navy uniform</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_ranks,_rates,_and_uniforms_of_the_18th_and_19th_centuries" title="Royal Navy ranks, rates, and uniforms of the 18th and 19th centuries">Royal Navy ranks, rates, and uniforms of the 18th and 19th centuries</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_officer_rank_insignia" title="Royal Navy officer rank insignia">Royal Navy officer rank insignia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_ratings_rank_insignia" title="Royal Navy ratings rank insignia">Royal Navy ratings rank insignia</a></div>
<p>The Royal Navy ranks, rates and insignia form part of the uniform of the Royal Navy. The Royal Navy uniform is the pattern on which many of the uniforms of the other national navies of the world are based (e.g. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ranks_and_insignia_of_NATO_navies_officers" title="Ranks and insignia of NATO navies officers">Ranks and insignia of NATO navies officers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uniforms_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Uniforms of the United States Navy">Uniforms of the United States Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uniforms_of_the_Royal_Canadian_Navy" title="Uniforms of the Royal Canadian Navy">Uniforms of the Royal Canadian Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Navy#Uniforms" title="French Navy">French Naval Uniforms</a>).</p>
<p>For officers (see also <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_officer_rank_insignia" title="Royal Navy officer rank insignia">Royal Navy officer rank insignia</a>):</p>
