<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Custom_and_tradition">Custom and tradition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Custom and tradition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_II_v_pd.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="210" data-file-width="220" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/8f/Elizabeth_II_v_pd.jpg" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_II_v_pd.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" title="Queen Elizabeth II">The Queen</a> and Admiral Sir Alan West during a <a href="/wiki/Fleet_review_(Commonwealth_realms)" title="Fleet review (Commonwealth realms)">Fleet Review</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Customs_and_traditions_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="Customs and traditions of the Royal Navy">Customs and traditions of the Royal Navy</a></div>
<p>The Royal Navy has several formal customs and traditions including the use of ensigns and ships badges. Royal Navy ships have several ensigns used when under way and when in port. Commissioned ships and submarines wear the <a href="/wiki/White_Ensign" title="White Ensign">White Ensign</a> at the stern whilst alongside during daylight hours and at the main-mast whilst under way. When alongside, the <i>Union Jack</i> is flown from the <a href="/wiki/Jackstaff" title="Jackstaff">jackstaff</a> at the bow, and can only be flown under way either to signal a court-martial is in progress or to indicate the presence of an admiral of the fleet on-board (including the Lord High Admiral or the monarch).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fleet_Review,_Royal_Navy" title="Fleet Review, Royal Navy">Fleet Review</a> is an irregular tradition of assembling the fleet before the monarch. The first review on record was held in 1400, and the most recent review as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> was held on 28 June 2005 to mark the bi-centenary of the Battle of Trafalgar; 167 ships from many different nations attended with the Royal Navy supplying 67.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are several less formal traditions including service nicknames and Naval slang. The nicknames include "The Andrew" (of uncertain origin, possibly after a zealous <a href="/wiki/Impressment" title="Impressment">press ganger</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[132]</a></sup> and "The Senior Service".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackspeak_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-jackspeak-138">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[134]</a></sup> The RN has evolved a rich volume of slang, known as "Jack-speak". Nowadays the British sailor is usually "Jack" (or "Jenny") rather than the more historical "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Tar" title="Jack Tar">Jack Tar</a>". Royal Marines are fondly known as "Bootnecks" or often just as "Royals". A compendium of Naval slang was brought together by Commander A. Covey-Crump and his name has in itself become the subject of Naval slang; <a href="/wiki/Covey_Crump" title="Covey Crump">Covey Crump</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackspeak_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-jackspeak-138">[133]</a></sup> A game traditionally played by the Navy is the four-player board game "<a href="/wiki/Uckers" title="Uckers">Uckers</a>". This is similar to <a href="/wiki/Ludo_(board_game)" title="Ludo (board game)">Ludo</a> and it is regarded as easy to learn, but difficult to play well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Navy_Cadets">Navy Cadets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Navy Cadets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Royal Navy sponsors or supports four youth organisations:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Volunteer_Cadet_Corps" title="Volunteer Cadet Corps">Volunteer Cadet Corps</a> - consisting of Royal Naval Cadets and Royal Marines Cadets, the VCC was the first youth organisation officially supported or sponsored by the Admiralty in 1901.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Combined_Cadet_Force" title="Combined Cadet Force">Combined Cadet Force</a> - consisting of Naval cadets although now under the operational command of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_Cadet_Corps" title="Sea Cadet Corps">Sea Cadet Corps</a> - consisting of Sea Cadets and Royal Marines Cadets, recognised by the Admiralty in 1919.</li>
<li>RN Recognised <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_Scouts" title="Sea Scouts">Sea Scouts</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>The above organisations are the responsibility of the CUY branch of Commander Core Training and Recruiting (COMCORE) who reports to <a href="/wiki/Flag_Officer_Sea_Training" title="Flag Officer Sea Training">Flag Officer Sea Training</a> (FOST).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Nautical_fiction" title="Nautical fiction">Nautical fiction</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(June 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The Royal Navy of the 18th century is depicted in many <a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty_(novel)" title="Mutiny on the Bounty (novel)">novels</a> and several films<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bounty_films_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-bounty_films-141">[136]</a></sup> dramatising the voyage and <a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty" title="Mutiny on the Bounty">mutiny on the Bounty</a>. The Royal Navy's Napoleonic campaigns of the early 19th century are a popular subject of historical novels. Some of the best-known are <a href="/wiki/Patrick_O%27Brian" title="Patrick O'Brian">Patrick O'Brian</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aubrey-Maturin_series" title="Aubrey-Maturin series">Aubrey-Maturin series</a>, <a href="/wiki/C._S._Forester" title="C. S. Forester">C. S. Forester</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Hornblower" title="Horatio Hornblower">Horatio Hornblower</a> chronicles, <a href="/wiki/Julian_Stockwin" title="Julian Stockwin">Julian Stockwin</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Kydd_(novel)" title="Kydd (novel)">Kydd</a> series, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Showell_Styles" title="Showell Styles">Showell Styles</a>' The Midshipman Quinn stories, <a href="/wiki/Dudley_Pope" title="Dudley Pope">Dudley Pope</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Lord_Ramage" title="Lord Ramage">Lord Ramage</a> novels and <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Reeman" title="Douglas Reeman">Douglas Reeman</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_Bolitho" title="Richard Bolitho">Richard Bolitho</a> novels. Other well-known novels include <a href="/wiki/Alistair_MacLean" title="Alistair MacLean">Alistair MacLean</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/HMS_Ulysses_(novel)" title="HMS Ulysses (novel)">HMS Ulysses</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Monsarrat" title="Nicholas Monsarrat">Nicholas Monsarrat</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Cruel_Sea_(book)" title="The Cruel Sea (book)">The Cruel Sea</a></i>, and C. S. Forester's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ship_(novel)" title="The Ship (novel)">The Ship</a></i>, all set during the Second World War.</p>
<p>The Navy can also be seen in numerous films. The fictional spy <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> is "officially" a commander in the Royal Navy. The Royal Navy is featured in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spy_Who_Loved_Me_(film)" title="The Spy Who Loved Me (film)">The Spy Who Loved Me</a></i>, when a nuclear ballistic-missile submarine is stolen, and in <i><a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Never_Dies" title="Tomorrow Never Dies">Tomorrow Never Dies</a></i> when a media baron sinks a Royal Navy warship in an attempt to trigger a war between the UK and People's Republic of China. <i><a href="/wiki/Master_and_Commander:_The_Far_Side_of_the_World" title="Master and Commander: The Far Side of the World">Master and Commander: The Far Side of the World</a></i> was based on Patrick O'Brian's Aubrey-Maturin series. The <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean" title="Pirates of the Caribbean">Pirates of the Caribbean</a></i> series of films also includes the Navy as the force pursuing the eponymous pirates. <a href="/wiki/No%C3%ABl_Coward" title="Noël Coward">Noël Coward</a> directed and starred in his own film <i><a href="/wiki/In_Which_We_Serve" title="In Which We Serve">In Which We Serve</a></i>, which tells the story of the crew of the fictional HMS <i>Torrin</i> during the Second World War. It was intended as a propaganda film and was released in 1942. Coward starred as the ship's <a href="/wiki/Captain_(naval)" title="Captain (naval)">captain</a>, with supporting roles from <a href="/wiki/John_Mills" title="John Mills">John Mills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Attenborough" title="Richard Attenborough">Richard Attenborough</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[137]</a></sup> Other examples of full-length feature films focusing specifically on the Royal Navy, have been: <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seagulls_over_Sorrento" title="Seagulls over Sorrento">Seagulls over Sorrento</a></i>; <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtse_Incident_(1957_film)" title="Yangtse Incident (1957 film)">Yangtse Incident</a></i>, the story of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Amethyst_(F116)" title="HMS Amethyst (F116)">HMS <i>Amethyst</i></a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s escape down the Yangtze river; <i><a href="/wiki/We_Dive_at_Dawn" title="We Dive at Dawn">We Dive at Dawn</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/The_Battle_of_the_River_Plate_(film)" title="The Battle of the River Plate (film)">The Battle of River Plate</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/Sink_the_Bismarck!" title="Sink the Bismarck!">Sink the Bismarck!</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/The_Navy_Lark_(film)" title="The Navy Lark (film)">The Navy Lark</a></i>.</p>
<p>C. S. Forester's Hornblower novels have been <a href="/wiki/Hornblower_(TV_series)" title="Hornblower (TV series)">adapted for television</a>, as have <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Cornwell" title="Bernard Cornwell">Bernard Cornwell</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Sharpe_(TV_series)" title="Sharpe (TV series)">Sharpe</a></i> series, which, although primarily involving the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a> of the time, includes several novels involving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_Sharpe_(fictional_character)" title="Richard Sharpe (fictional character)">Richard Sharpe</a> at sea with the Navy. The Royal Navy was the subject of an acclaimed 1970s <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> television drama series, <i><a href="/wiki/Warship_(TV_series)" title="Warship (TV series)">Warship</a></i>, and of a five-part documentary, <i>Shipmates</i>, that followed the workings of the Royal Navy day to day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>Television documentaries about the Royal Navy include: <i>Empire of the Seas: How the Navy Forged the Modern World</i>, a four-part documentary depicting Britain's rise as a naval superpower, up until the First World War; <i><a href="/wiki/Sailor_(TV_series)" title="Sailor (TV series)">Sailor</a></i>, about life on the aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ark_Royal_(R09)" title="HMS Ark Royal (R09)">HMS <i>Ark Royal</i></a>; and <i>Submarine</i>, about the <a href="/wiki/Submarine_Command_Course" title="Submarine Command Course">submarine captains' training course</a>, 'The Perisher'. A book based on the series, and also called <i>Submarine</i>, was produced by Jonathan Crane. There have also been recent Channel 5 documentaries such as <i>Royal Navy Submarine Patrol</i>, following a nuclear-powered fleet submarine.</p>
<p>The popular BBC radio comedy series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Navy_Lark" title="The Navy Lark">The Navy Lark</a></i> featured a fictitious warship ("HMS <i>Troutbridge</i>") and ran from 1959 to 1977.</p>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">4 November</span> 2006</span>. <q>Britannia, with her shield and trident, is the very symbol, not only of the Royal Navy, but also of British global power. In the last instance, the Royal Navy is the United Kingdom's greatest strategic asset and instrument. As the only other 'blue-water' navy other than those of France and the United States, its ballistic missile submarines carry the nation's nuclear deterrent and its aircraft carriers and escorting naval squadrons supply London with a deep oceanic power projection capability, which enables Britain to maintain a 'forward presence' globally, and the ability to influence events tactically throughout the world.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARoyal+Navy&amp;rft.btitle=The+Royal+Navy%3A+Britain%E2%80%99s+Trident+for+a+Global+Agenda&amp;rft.date=2006-11-04&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.pub=Henry+Jackson+Society&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fhenryjacksonsociety.org%2F2006%2F11%2F04%2Fthe-royal-navy-britains-trident-for-a-global-agenda%2F&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
